//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/US-MarshallPlanAid-Logo.svg/400px-US-MarshallPlanAid-Logo.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The labeling used on <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">aid</a> to Western Europe</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marshall_Plan.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="422" data-file-width="428" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Marshall_Plan.png/200px-Marshall_Plan.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Marshall_Plan.png/300px-Marshall_Plan.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Marshall_Plan.png/400px-Marshall_Plan.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Map of Cold War-era Europe and the <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near East</a> showing countries that received Marshall Plan aid. The red columns show the relative amount of total aid received per nation.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marshallplanhilfe.gif"><img alt="" data-file-height="1960" data-file-width="1849" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Marshallplanhilfe.gif/200px-Marshallplanhilfe.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Marshallplanhilfe.gif/300px-Marshallplanhilfe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Marshallplanhilfe.gif/400px-Marshallplanhilfe.gif 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Construction in <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> under Marshall Plan aid</div></div></div></div>\n<p>In early 1947, France, Britain and the United States unsuccessfully attempted to reach an agreement with the Soviet Union for a plan envisioning an economically self-sufficient Germany, including a detailed accounting of the industrial plants, goods and infrastructure already removed by the Soviets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller16_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-miller16-88">[88]</a></sup> In June 1947, in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Truman_Doctrine" title="Truman Doctrine">Truman Doctrine</a>, the United States enacted the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a>, a pledge of economic assistance for all European countries willing to participate, including the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller16_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-miller16-88">[88]</a></sup> Under the plan, which President Harry S. Truman signed on 3 April 1948, the US government gave to Western European countries over $13 billion (equivalent to $189.39 billion in 2016) to rebuild the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Europe" title="Economy of Europe">economy of Europe</a>. Later, the program led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/OECD#Organisation_for_European_Economic_Co-operation" title="OECD">Organisation for European Economic Co-operation</a>.\n</p><p>The plan\'s aim was to rebuild the democratic and economic systems of Europe and to counter perceived threats to <a href="/wiki/European_balance_of_power" title="European balance of power">Europe\'s balance of power</a>, such as communist parties seizing control through revolutions or elections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The plan also stated that European prosperity was contingent upon German economic recovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> One month later, Truman signed the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Act_of_1947" title="National Security Act of 1947">National Security Act of 1947</a>, creating a unified <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">Department of Defense</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA), and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council" title="United States National Security Council">National Security Council</a> (NSC). These would become the main bureaucracies for US defense policy in the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stalin believed that economic integration with the West would allow <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries to escape Soviet control, and that the US was trying to buy a pro-US re-alignment of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis32_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis32-92">[92]</a></sup> Stalin therefore prevented Eastern Bloc nations from receiving Marshall Plan aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis32_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis32-92">[92]</a></sup> The Soviet Union\'s alternative to the Marshall Plan, which was purported to involve Soviet subsidies and trade with central and eastern Europe, became known as the <a href="/wiki/Molotov_Plan" title="Molotov Plan">Molotov Plan</a> (later institutionalized in January 1949 as the <a href="/wiki/Comecon" title="Comecon">Council for Mutual Economic Assistance</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup> Stalin was also fearful of a reconstituted Germany; his vision of a post-war Germany did not include the ability to rearm or pose any kind of threat to the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early 1948, following reports of strengthening "reactionary elements", Soviet operatives executed a <a href="/wiki/1948_Czechoslovak_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1948 Czechoslovak coup d\'&#233;tat">coup d\'&#233;tat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, the only Eastern Bloc state that the Soviets had permitted to retain democratic structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wettig86_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-wettig86-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The public brutality of the coup shocked Western powers more than any event up to that point, set in a motion a brief scare that war would occur and swept away the last vestiges of opposition to the Marshall Plan in the United States Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller19_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-miller19-96">[96]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The twin policies of the Truman Doctrine and the Marshall Plan led to billions in economic and military aid for Western Europe, Greece, and Turkey. With the US assistance, the Greek military <a href="/wiki/Greek_Civil_War" title="Greek Civil War">won its civil war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup> Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Alcide_De_Gasperi" title="Alcide De Gasperi">Alcide De Gasperi</a> the Italian <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democracy_(Italy)" title="Christian Democracy (Italy)">Christian Democrats</a> defeated the powerful <a href="/wiki/Italian_Communist_Party" title="Italian Communist Party">Communist</a>&#8211;<a href="/wiki/Italian_Socialist_Party" title="Italian Socialist Party">Socialist</a> alliance in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_general_election,_1948" title="Italian general election, 1948">elections of 1948</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Espionage">Espionage</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_espionage" title="Cold War espionage">Cold War espionage</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_espionage_in_the_Soviet_Union_and_Russian_Federation" title="American espionage in the Soviet Union and Russian Federation">American espionage in the Soviet Union and Russian Federation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_espionage_in_the_United_States" title="Soviet espionage in the United States">Soviet espionage in the United States</a></div>\n<p>All major powers engaged in espionage, using a great variety of spies, double agents, and new technologies such as the tapping of telephone cables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>  The most famous and active organizations were the American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA" title="CIA">CIA</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> the Soviet <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a>, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and the British <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MI6" title="MI6">MI6</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>  The East German <a href="/wiki/Stasi" title="Stasi">Stasi</a>, unlike the others, was primarily concerned with internal security, but its <a href="/wiki/Main_Directorate_for_Reconnaissance" title="Main Directorate for Reconnaissance">Main Directorate for Reconnaissance</a> operated espionage activities around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>  The CIA secretly subsidized and promoted anti-communist cultural activities and organizations. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The CIA was also involved in European politics, especially in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>  Espionage took place all over the world, but Berlin was the most important battleground for spying activity. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>So much top secret archival information has been released so that historian <a href="/wiki/Raymond_L._Garthoff" title="Raymond L. Garthoff">Raymond L. Garthoff</a> concludes there probably was parity in the quantity and quality of secret information obtained by each side. However, the Soviets probably had an advantage in terms of HUMINT (espionage) and "sometimes in its reach into high policy circles."  In terms of decisive impact, however, he concludes:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>We also can now have high confidence in the judgment that there were no successful &#8220;moles&#8221; at the political decision-making level on either side.  Similarly, there is no evidence, on either side, of any major political or military decision that was prematurely discovered through espionage and  thwarted by the other side. There also is no evidence of any major political or military decision that was crucially influenced (much less generated) by an agent of the other side.</dd></dl>\n<p>In addition to usual espionage, the Western agencies paid special attention to debriefing <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_emigration_and_defection" title="Eastern Bloc emigration and defection">Eastern Bloc defectors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Cominform_and_the_Tito.E2.80.93Stalin_Split"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cominform_and_the_Tito&#8211;Stalin_Split">Cominform and the Tito&#8211;Stalin Split</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cominform" title="Cominform">Cominform</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tito%E2%80%93Stalin_Split" title="Tito&#8211;Stalin Split">Tito&#8211;Stalin Split</a></div>\n<p>In September 1947, the Soviets created <a href="/wiki/Cominform" title="Cominform">Cominform</a>, the purpose of which was to enforce orthodoxy within the international communist movement and tighten political control over Soviet <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">satellites</a> through coordination of communist parties in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis32_92-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis32-92">[92]</a></sup> Cominform faced an embarrassing setback the following June, when the <a href="/wiki/Tito%E2%80%93Stalin_Split" title="Tito&#8211;Stalin Split">Tito&#8211;Stalin Split</a> obliged its members to expel Yugoslavia, which remained communist but adopted a <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">non-aligned</a> position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Berlin_Blockade_and_Airlift">Berlin Blockade and Airlift</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">Berlin Blockade</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1438" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg/220px-C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg/330px-C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg/440px-C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C-47s_at_Tempelhof_Airport_Berlin_1948.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>C-47s unloading at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tempelhof_Airport" title="Berlin Tempelhof Airport">Tempelhof Airport</a> in Berlin during the Berlin Blockade</div></div></div>\n<p>The United States and Britain merged their western German occupation zones into <a href="/wiki/Bizone" title="Bizone">"Bizonia"</a> (1 January 1947, later "Trizonia" with the addition of France\'s zone, April 1949).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller13_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-miller13-109">[109]</a></sup> As part of the economic rebuilding of Germany, in early 1948, representatives of a number of Western European governments and the United States announced an agreement for a merger of western German areas into a federal governmental system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller18_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-miller18-110">[110]</a></sup> In addition, in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a>, they began to re-industrialize and rebuild the German economy, including the introduction of a new <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Mark" title="Deutsche Mark">Deutsche Mark</a> currency to replace the old <a href="/wiki/Reichsmark" title="Reichsmark">Reichsmark</a> currency that the Soviets had debased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller31_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-miller31-111">[111]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shortly thereafter, Stalin instituted the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade" title="Berlin Blockade">Berlin Blockade</a> (24 June 1948 &#8211; 12 May 1949), one of the first major crises of the Cold War, preventing food, materials and supplies from arriving in <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The United States, Britain, France, Canada, Australia, New Zealand and several other countries began the massive "Berlin airlift", supplying West Berlin with food and other provisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Soviets mounted a public relations campaign against the policy change. Once again the East Berlin communists attempted to disrupt the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Blockade#December_elections" title="Berlin Blockade">Berlin municipal elections</a> (as they had done in the 1946 elections),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller13_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-miller13-109">[109]</a></sup> which were held on 5 December 1948 and produced a turnout of 86.3% and an overwhelming victory for the non-communist parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The results effectively divided the city into East and West versions of its former self. 300,000 Berliners demonstrated and urged the international airlift to continue,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> and US Air Force pilot <a href="/wiki/Gail_Halvorsen" title="Gail Halvorsen">Gail Halvorsen</a> created "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Vittles" title="Operation Vittles">Operation Vittles</a>", which supplied candy to German children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller26_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-miller26-116">[116]</a></sup> In May 1949, Stalin backed down and lifted the blockade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._34_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._34-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1952, Stalin repeatedly <a href="/wiki/Stalin_Note" title="Stalin Note">proposed a plan</a> to unify East and West Germany under a single government chosen in elections supervised by the United Nations, if the new Germany were to stay out of Western military alliances, but this proposal was turned down by the Western powers. Some sources dispute the sincerity of the proposal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings_of_NATO_and_Radio_Free_Europe">Beginnings of NATO and Radio Free Europe</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_media_and_propaganda" title="Eastern Bloc media and propaganda">Eastern Bloc media and propaganda</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2359" data-file-width="2968" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg/220px-Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg/330px-Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg/440px-Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Truman_signing_North_Atlantic_Treaty.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Truman signs the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a> with guests in the Oval Office.</div></div></div>\n<p>Britain, France, the United States, Canada and other eight western European countries signed the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty" title="North Atlantic Treaty">North Atlantic Treaty</a> of April 1949, establishing the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization</a> (NATO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._34_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._34-63">[63]</a></sup> That August, the <a href="/wiki/RDS-1" title="RDS-1">first Soviet atomic device</a> was detonated in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semipalatinsk" title="Semipalatinsk">Semipalatinsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic">Kazakh SSR</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup> Following Soviet refusals to participate in a German rebuilding effort set forth by western European countries in 1948,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-miller18_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-miller18-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-turner23_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-turner23-119">[119]</a></sup> the US, Britain and France spearheaded the establishment of West Germany from the <a href="/wiki/Bizone" title="Bizone">three Western zones of occupation</a> in April 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The Soviet Union proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone" title="Soviet occupation zone">its zone of occupation</a> in Germany the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">German Democratic Republic</a> that October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byrd_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Byrd-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Media in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> was an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_media_and_propaganda" title="Eastern Bloc media and propaganda">organ of the state</a>, completely reliant on and subservient to the communist party. Radio and television organizations were state-owned, while print media was usually owned by political organizations, mostly by the local communist party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneil15_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-oneil15-121">[121]</a></sup> Soviet propaganda used Marxist philosophy to attack capitalism, claiming labor exploitation and war-mongering imperialism were inherent in the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Along with the broadcasts of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">British Broadcasting Corporation</a> (BBC) and the <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a> to Central and Eastern Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> a major propaganda effort begun in 1949 was <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a>, dedicated to bringing about the peaceful demise of the communist system in the Eastern Bloc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puddington9_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington9-124">[124]</a></sup> Radio Free Europe attempted to achieve these goals by serving as a surrogate home radio station, an alternative to the controlled and party-dominated domestic press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puddington9_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington9-124">[124]</a></sup> Radio Free Europe was a product of some of the most prominent architects of America\'s early Cold War strategy, especially those who believed that the Cold War would eventually be fought by political rather than military means, such as George F. Kennan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puddington7_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington7-125">[125]</a></sup>\n</p><p>American policymakers, including Kennan and <a href="/wiki/John_Foster_Dulles" title="John Foster Dulles">John Foster Dulles</a>, acknowledged that the Cold War was in its essence a war of ideas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puddington7_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Puddington7-125">[125]</a></sup> The United States, acting through the CIA, funded a long list of projects to counter the communist appeal among intellectuals in Europe and the developing world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The CIA also <a href="/wiki/Secrecy" title="Secrecy">covertly</a> sponsored a domestic propaganda campaign called <a href="/wiki/Crusade_for_Freedom" title="Crusade for Freedom">Crusade for Freedom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early 1950s, the US worked for the rearmament of West Germany and, in 1955, secured its full membership of NATO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byrd_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-Byrd-47">[47]</a></sup> In May 1953, Beria, by then in a government post, had made an unsuccessful proposal to allow the reunification of a neutral Germany to prevent West Germany\'s incorporation into NATO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_Civil_War_and_SEATO">Chinese Civil War and SEATO</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia_Treaty_Organization" title="Southeast Asia Treaty Organization">Southeast Asia Treaty Organization</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mao,_Bulganin,_Stalin,_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="297" data-file-width="466" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg/220px-Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg/330px-Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg/440px-Mao%2C_Bulganin%2C_Stalin%2C_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mao,_Bulganin,_Stalin,_Ulbricht_Tsedenbal.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mao Zedong and Joseph Stalin in Moscow, December 1949</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1949, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People\'s Liberation Army">People\'s Liberation Army</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>\'s United States-backed <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) Nationalist Government in China, and the Soviet Union promptly created an alliance with the newly formed People\'s Republic of China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> According to Norwegian historian <a href="/wiki/Odd_Arne_Westad" title="Odd Arne Westad">Odd Arne Westad</a>, the communists won the Civil War because they made fewer military mistakes than Chiang Kai-Shek made, and because in his search for a powerful centralized government, Chiang antagonized too many interest groups in China. Moreover, his party was weakened during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">war against Japan</a>. Meanwhile, the communists told different groups, such as the peasants, exactly what they wanted to hear, and they cloaked themselves under the cover of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_nationalism" title="Chinese nationalism">Chinese nationalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Chiang and his KMT government retreated to the island of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>. Confronted with the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Revolution" title="Chinese Communist Revolution">communist revolution in China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet_atomic_bomb_project" title="Soviet atomic bomb project">the end of the American atomic monopoly in 1949</a>, the Truman administration quickly moved to escalate and expand its <a href="/wiki/Containment" title="Containment">containment</a> policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/NSC_68" title="NSC 68">NSC 68</a>, a secret 1950 document,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._164_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._164-131">[131]</a></sup> the National Security Council proposed to reinforce pro-Western alliance systems and quadruple spending on defense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-4"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>United States officials moved thereafter to expand containment into <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, in order to counter revolutionary nationalist movements, often led by communist parties financed by the USSR, fighting against the restoration of Europe\'s colonial empires in South-East Asia and elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._212_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._212-132">[132]</a></sup> In the early 1950s (a period sometimes known as the "<a href="/wiki/Pactomania" title="Pactomania">Pactomania</a>"), the US formalized a series of alliances with <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> (notably <a href="/wiki/ANZUS" title="ANZUS">ANZUS</a> in 1951 and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia_Treaty_Organization" title="Southeast Asia Treaty Organization">SEATO</a> in 1954), thereby guaranteeing the United States a number of long-term military bases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byrd_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-Byrd-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Korean_War">Korean War</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2331" data-file-width="2837" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg/220px-IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg/330px-IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg/440px-IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IncheonLandingMcArthur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a>, UN Command CiC (seated), observes the naval shelling of <a href="/wiki/Incheon" title="Incheon">Incheon</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USS_Mount_McKinley_(AGC-7)" title="USS Mount McKinley (AGC-7)">USS <i>Mt. McKinley</i></a>, 15 September 1950</div></div></div>\n<p>One of the more significant examples of the implementation of containment was US intervention in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>. In June 1950, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Il-sung" title="Kim Il-sung">Kim Il-sung</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Korean_People%27s_Army" title="Korean People\'s Army">North Korean People\'s Army</a> invaded South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stokesbury1990_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stokesbury1990-133">[133]</a></sup> Stalin approved and sent advisers to plan the North Korean invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeathersby199328,_30_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeathersby199328,_30-134">[134]</a></sup> To Stalin\'s surprise,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> backed the defense of South Korea, though the Soviets were then boycotting meetings in protest that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Taiwan</a> and not <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">Communist China</a> held a permanent seat on the Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Command" title="United Nations Command">UN force</a> of personnel from South Korea, the United States, the United Kingdom, Turkey, Canada, Colombia, Australia, France, South Africa, the Philippines, the Netherlands, Belgium, New Zealand and other countries joined to stop the invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4597" data-file-width="5773" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg/200px-KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg/300px-KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg/400px-KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KoreanWar_recover_Seoul.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Marines" title="U.S. Marines">U.S. Marines</a> engaged in street fighting during the liberation of <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, September 1950</div></div></div>\n<p>Among other effects, the Korean War galvanised <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> to develop a military structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Public opinion in countries involved, such as Great Britain, was divided for and against the war. Many feared an escalation into a general war with Communist China, and even nuclear war. The strong opposition to the war often strained <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="United Kingdom&#8211;United States relations">Anglo-American relations</a>. For these reasons British officials sought a speedy end to the conflict, hoping to unite Korea under United Nations auspices and for withdrawal of all foreign forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Even though the Chinese and North Koreans were exhausted by the war and were prepared to end it by late 1952, Stalin insisted that they continue fighting, and the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Armistice_Agreement" title="Korean Armistice Agreement">Armistice</a> was approved only in July 1953, after Stalin\'s death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byrd_47-4"><a href="#cite_note-Byrd-47">[47]</a></sup> North Korean leader Kim Il Sung created a highly centralized, <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">totalitarian</a> dictatorship&#8212;which continues to date&#8212;according himself unlimited power and generating a formidable <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In the South, the American-backed <a href="/wiki/Strongman_(politics)" title="Strongman (politics)">strongman</a> <a href="/wiki/Syngman_Rhee" title="Syngman Rhee">Syngman Rhee</a> ran a significantly less brutal but deeply <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corrupt</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authoritarian" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> After Rhee was overthrown in 1960, South Korea fell within a year under a period of military rule that lasted until the re-establishment of a multi-party system in the late 1980s.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Crisis_and_escalation_.281953.E2.80.931962.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Crisis_and_escalation_(1953&#8211;1962)">Crisis and escalation (1953&#8211;1962)</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_(1953%E2%80%931962)" title="Cold War (1953&#8211;1962)">Cold War (1953&#8211;1962)</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Khrushchev.2C_Eisenhower_and_de-Stalinization"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Khrushchev,_Eisenhower_and_de-Stalinization">Khrushchev, Eisenhower and de-Stalinization</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="689" data-file-width="655" decoding="async" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/220px-1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/330px-1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/440px-1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1959_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NATO and Warsaw Pact troop strengths in Europe in 1959</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1953, changes in political leadership on both sides shifted the dynamic of the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-142">[142]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> was inaugurated president that January. During the last 18&#160;months of the Truman administration, the American defense budget had quadrupled, and Eisenhower moved to reduce military spending by a third while continuing to fight the Cold War effectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-6"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the death of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> became the Soviet leader following the deposition and execution of <a href="/wiki/Lavrentiy_Beria" title="Lavrentiy Beria">Lavrentiy Beria</a> and the pushing aside of rivals <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Malenkov" title="Georgy Malenkov">Georgy Malenkov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vyacheslav_Molotov" title="Vyacheslav Molotov">Vyacheslav Molotov</a>. On 25 February 1956, Khrushchev shocked delegates to the <a href="/wiki/20th_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="20th Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">20th Congress</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Soviet Communist Party</a> by <a href="/wiki/On_the_Cult_of_Personality_and_Its_Consequences" title="On the Cult of Personality and Its Consequences">cataloguing and denouncing Stalin\'s crimes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> As part of a campaign of <a href="/wiki/De-Stalinization" title="De-Stalinization">de-Stalinization</a>, he declared that the only way to reform and move away from Stalin\'s policies would be to acknowledge errors made in the past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 November 1956, while addressing Western ambassadors at a reception at the Polish embassy in Moscow, Khrushchev used his famous "Whether you like it or not, history is on our side. <a href="/wiki/We_will_bury_you" title="We will bury you">We will bury you</a>" expression, shocking everyone present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> He later claimed that he had not been talking about nuclear war, but rather about the historically determined victory of communism over capitalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In 1961, Khrushchev declared that even if the USSR was behind the West, within a decade its housing shortage would disappear, consumer goods would be abundant, and within two decades, the "construction of a communist society" in the USSR would be completed "in the main".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Eisenhower\'s secretary of state, John Foster Dulles, initiated a "<a href="/wiki/New_Look_(policy)" title="New Look (policy)">New Look</a>" for the <a href="/wiki/Containment" title="Containment">containment</a> strategy, calling for a greater reliance on nuclear weapons against US enemies in wartime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup> Dulles also enunciated the doctrine of "<a href="/wiki/Massive_retaliation" title="Massive retaliation">massive retaliation</a>", threatening a severe US response to any Soviet aggression. Possessing nuclear superiority, for example, allowed Eisenhower to face down Soviet threats to intervene in the Middle East during the 1956 <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-7"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup> US plans for nuclear war in the late 1950s included the "systematic destruction" of 1,200 major urban centers in the Eastern Bloc and China, including Moscow, East Berlin and Beijing, with their civilian populations among the primary targets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Warsaw_Pact_and_Hungarian_Revolution">Warsaw Pact and Hungarian Revolution</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">Hungarian Revolution of 1956</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">The Hungarian Revolution of 1956</div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n,_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3103" data-file-width="4840" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg/220px-Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg/330px-Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg/440px-Kossuth_Lajos_utca_a_Ferenciek_tere_fel%C5%91l_n%C3%A9zve._1956._okt%C3%B3ber_25-e_d%C3%A9lut%C3%A1n%2C_-_Fortepan_24652.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">March of protesters in Budapest, on 25 October;</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1552" data-file-width="2243" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg/220px-Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg/330px-Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg/440px-Sz%C3%A9tl%C5%91tt_harckocsi_a_M%C3%B3ricz_Zsigmond_k%C3%B6rt%C3%A9ren.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A destroyed Soviet T-34-85 tank in Budapest</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_empire_1960.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/220px-Soviet_empire_1960.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/330px-Soviet_empire_1960.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soviet_empire_1960.png/440px-Soviet_empire_1960.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soviet_empire_1960.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The maximum territorial extent of countries in the world under Soviet <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">influence</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> of 1959 and before the official <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a> of 1961</div></div></div>\n<p>While <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Stalin</a>\'s death in 1953 slightly relaxed tensions, the situation in Europe remained an uneasy armed truce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palmowski_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Palmowski-148">[148]</a></sup> The Soviets, who had already created a network of mutual assistance treaties in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> by 1949,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> established a formal alliance therein, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>, in 1955.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byrd_47-5"><a href="#cite_note-Byrd-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1956" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1956">Hungarian Revolution of 1956</a> occurred shortly after Khrushchev arranged the removal of Hungary\'s Stalinist leader <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ty%C3%A1s_R%C3%A1kosi" title="M&#225;ty&#225;s R&#225;kosi">M&#225;ty&#225;s R&#225;kosi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In response to a popular uprising,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> the new regime formally disbanded the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%81VH" title="&#193;VH">secret police</a>, declared its intention to withdraw from the Warsaw Pact and pledged to re-establish free elections. The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Army" title="Soviet Army">Soviet Army</a> invaded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-troops_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-troops-152">[152]</a></sup> Thousands of Hungarians were arrested, imprisoned and deported to the Soviet Union,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> and approximately 200,000 Hungarians fled Hungary in the chaos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cseresneyes_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cseresneyes-154">[154]</a></sup> Hungarian leader <a href="/wiki/Imre_Nagy" title="Imre Nagy">Imre Nagy</a> and others were executed following secret trials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCJune16_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCJune16-155">[155]</a></sup>\nFrom 1957 through 1961, Khrushchev openly and repeatedly threatened the West with nuclear annihilation. He claimed that Soviet missile capabilities were far superior to those of the United States, capable of wiping out any American or European city. However, Khrushchev rejected Stalin\'s belief in the inevitability of war, and declared his new goal was to be "<a href="/wiki/Peaceful_coexistence" title="Peaceful coexistence">peaceful coexistence</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> This formulation modified the Stalin-era Soviet stance, where international <a href="/wiki/Class_conflict" title="Class conflict">class conflict</a> meant the two opposing camps were on an inevitable collision course where communism would triumph through global war; now, peace would allow capitalism to collapse on its own,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> as well as giving the Soviets time to boost their military capabilities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> which remained for decades until Gorbachev\'s later "new thinking" envisioning peaceful coexistence as an end in itself rather than a form of class struggle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The events in Hungary produced ideological fractures within the communist parties of the world, particularly in Western Europe, with great decline in membership as many in both western and communist countries felt disillusioned by the brutal Soviet response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lendvai196_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lendvai196-160">[160]</a></sup> The communist parties in the West would never recover from the effect the Hungarian Revolution had on their membership, a fact that was immediately recognized by some, such as the Yugoslavian politician <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milovan_Djilas" title="Milovan Djilas">Milovan &#272;ilas</a> who shortly after the revolution was crushed said that "The wound which the Hungarian Revolution inflicted on communism can never be completely healed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lendvai196_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lendvai196-160">[160]</a></sup>\n</p><p>America\'s pronouncements concentrated on American strength abroad and the success of liberal capitalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> However, by the late 1960s, the "battle for men\'s minds" between two systems of social organization that Kennedy spoke of in 1961 was largely over, with tensions henceforth based primarily on clashing geopolitical objectives rather than ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Berlin_ultimatum_and_European_integration">Berlin ultimatum and European integration</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Crisis_of_1961#Berlin_ultimatum" title="Berlin Crisis of 1961">Berlin Crisis of 1961 &#167;&#160;Berlin ultimatum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a></div>\n<p>During November 1958, Khrushchev made an unsuccessful attempt to turn all of Berlin into an independent, demilitarized "free city". He gave the United States, Great Britain, and France a six-month ultimatum to withdraw their troops from the sectors they still occupied in West Berlin, or he would transfer control of Western access rights to the East Germans. Khrushchev earlier explained to <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> that "Berlin is the testicles of the West. Every time I want to make the West scream, I squeeze on Berlin."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> NATO formally rejected the ultimatum in mid-December and Khrushchev withdrew it in return for a Geneva conference on the German question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>\n</p><p>More broadly, one hallmark of the 1950s was the beginning of <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>&#8212;a fundamental by-product of the Cold War. Truman and Eisenhower promoted the concept politically, economically, and militarily, but later administrations viewed it ambivalently, fearful that an independent Europe would forge a separate d&#233;tente with the Soviet Union, which would use this to exacerbate Western disunity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_in_the_Third_World">Competition in the Third World</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Decolonization#After_1945" title="Decolonization">Decolonization &#167;&#160;After 1945</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_national_liberation" title="Wars of national liberation">Wars of national liberation</a>, <a href="/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1953 Iranian coup d\'&#233;tat">1953 Iranian coup d\'&#233;tat</a>, <a href="/wiki/1954_Guatemalan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1954 Guatemalan coup d\'&#233;tat">1954 Guatemalan coup d\'&#233;tat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonization_1945.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/290px-Colonization_1945.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/435px-Colonization_1945.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/580px-Colonization_1945.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonization_1945.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Western <a href="/wiki/Colonial_empire" title="Colonial empire">colonial empires</a> in Asia and Africa all collapsed in the years after 1945.</div></div></div>\n<p>Nationalist movements in some countries and regions, notably <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, Indonesia and <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a>, were often allied with communist groups or perceived in the West to be allied with communists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-4"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup> In this context, the United States and the Soviet Union increasingly competed for influence by proxy in the Third World as <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> gained momentum in the 1950s and early 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Additionally, the Soviets saw continuing losses by imperial powers as presaging the eventual victory of their ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Both sides were selling armaments to gain influence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1961_CPA_2566_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="810" data-file-width="817" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/1961_CPA_2566_%281%29.jpg/170px-1961_CPA_2566_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/1961_CPA_2566_%281%29.jpg/255px-1961_CPA_2566_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/1961_CPA_2566_%281%29.jpg/340px-1961_CPA_2566_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1961_CPA_2566_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1961 Soviet postage stamp demanding freedom for African nations</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1961_CPA_2576.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1535" data-file-width="1122" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/1961_CPA_2576.jpg/170px-1961_CPA_2576.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/1961_CPA_2576.jpg/255px-1961_CPA_2576.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/1961_CPA_2576.jpg/340px-1961_CPA_2576.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1961_CPA_2576.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1961 Soviet stamp commemorating <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a>, prime minister of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)">Republic of the Congo</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The United States used the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> (CIA) to do away with a string of unfriendly Third World governments and to support allied ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-5"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup> In 1953, President Eisenhower\'s CIA implemented <a href="/wiki/1953_Iranian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat#Execution_of_Operation_Ajax" title="1953 Iranian coup d\'&#233;tat">Operation Ajax</a>, a covert operation aimed at overthrowing the Iranian prime minister, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Mosaddegh" title="Mohammad Mosaddegh">Mohammad Mosaddegh</a>. The popularly elected and non-aligned Mosaddegh had been a Middle Eastern nemesis of Britain since nationalizing the British-owned <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Persian_Oil_Company" title="Anglo-Persian Oil Company">Anglo-Iranian Oil Company</a> in 1951. <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> told the United States that Mosaddegh was "increasingly turning towards communism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The pro-Western <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">shah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">Mohammad Reza Pahlavi</a>, assumed control as an <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocratic</a> monarch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> The shah\'s policies included banning the communist <a href="/wiki/Tudeh_Party_of_Iran" title="Tudeh Party of Iran">Tudeh Party of Iran</a>, and general suppression of political dissent by <a href="/wiki/SAVAK" title="SAVAK">SAVAK</a>, the shah\'s domestic security and intelligence agency.\n</p><p>In Guatemala, a <a href="/wiki/1954_Guatemalan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1954 Guatemalan coup d\'&#233;tat">CIA-backed military coup</a> ousted the left-wing President <a href="/wiki/Jacobo_%C3%81rbenz" title="Jacobo &#193;rbenz">Jacobo &#193;rbenz</a> in 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> The post-Arbenz government&#8212;a <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military junta</a> headed by <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Castillo_Armas" title="Carlos Castillo Armas">Carlos Castillo Armas</a>&#8212;repealed a <a href="/wiki/Decree_900" title="Decree 900">progressive land reform law</a>, returned nationalized property belonging to the <a href="/wiki/United_Fruit_Company" title="United Fruit Company">United Fruit Company</a>, set up a <a href="/wiki/National_Committee_of_Defense_Against_Communism" title="National Committee of Defense Against Communism">National Committee of Defense Against Communism</a>, and decreed a <a href="/wiki/Preventive_Penal_Law_Against_Communism" title="Preventive Penal Law Against Communism">Preventive Penal Law Against Communism</a> at the request of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The non-aligned Indonesian government of <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> was faced with a major threat to its legitimacy beginning in 1956, when several regional commanders began to demand autonomy from <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>. After mediation failed, Sukarno took action to remove the dissident commanders. In February 1958, dissident military commanders in Central Sumatera (Colonel Ahmad Hussein) and North Sulawesi (Colonel Ventje Sumual) declared the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Government_of_the_Republic_of_Indonesia" title="Revolutionary Government of the Republic of Indonesia">Revolutionary Government of the Republic of Indonesia</a>-<a href="/wiki/Permesta" title="Permesta">Permesta</a> Movement aimed at overthrowing the Sukarno regime. They were joined by many civilian politicians from the <a href="/wiki/Masyumi_Party" title="Masyumi Party">Masyumi Party</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Sjafruddin_Prawiranegara" title="Sjafruddin Prawiranegara">Sjafruddin Prawiranegara</a>, who were opposed to the growing influence of the communist <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Indonesia" title="Communist Party of Indonesia">Partai Komunis Indonesia</a> party. Due to their anti-communist rhetoric, the rebels received arms, funding, and other covert aid from the CIA until <a href="/wiki/Allen_Lawrence_Pope" title="Allen Lawrence Pope">Allen Lawrence Pope</a>, an American pilot, was shot down after a bombing raid on government-held <a href="/wiki/Ambon,_Maluku" title="Ambon, Maluku">Ambon</a> in April 1958. The central government responded by launching airborne and seaborne military invasions of rebel strongholds <a href="/wiki/Padang" title="Padang">Padang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manado" title="Manado">Manado</a>. By the end of 1958, the rebels were militarily defeated, and the last remaining rebel guerilla bands surrendered by August 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (L&#233;opoldville)">Republic of the Congo</a>, newly independent from <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> since June 1960, the CIA-cultivated President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kasa-Vubu" title="Joseph Kasa-Vubu">Joseph Kasa-Vubu</a> ordered the dismissal of the democratically elected Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">Patrice Lumumba</a> and the Lumumba cabinet in September; Lumumba called for Kasa-Vubu\'s dismissal instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schraeder_1994,_57_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schraeder_1994,_57-177">[177]</a></sup> In the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a>, the CIA-backed Colonel <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> quickly mobilized his forces to seize power through a military coup d\'&#233;tat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schraeder_1994,_57_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schraeder_1994,_57-177">[177]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif/220px-African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif/330px-African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif/440px-African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:African_nations_order_of_independence_1950-1993.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An animated map shows the order of <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa" title="Decolonisation of Africa">independence of the African nations</a>, 1950&#8211;2011</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a>, the leftist <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Progressive_Party_(Guyana)" title="People\'s Progressive Party (Guyana)">People\'s Progressive Party</a> (PPP) candidate <a href="/wiki/Cheddi_Jagan" title="Cheddi Jagan">Cheddi Jagan</a> won the position of chief minister in a colonially administered election in 1953, but was quickly forced to resign from power after Britain\'s suspension of the still-dependent nation\'s constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rose_2002,_167_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rose_2002,_167-178">[178]</a></sup> Embarrassed by the landslide electoral victory of Jagan\'s allegedly Marxist party, the British imprisoned the PPP\'s leadership and maneuvered the organization into a divisive rupture in 1955, engineering a split between Jagan and his PPP colleagues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mars_&amp;_Young_2004,_xviii_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mars_&amp;_Young_2004,_xviii-179">[179]</a></sup> Jagan again won the colonial elections in 1957 and 1961; despite Britain\'s shift to a reconsideration of its view of the left-wing Jagan as a Soviet-style communist at this time, the United States pressured the British to withhold <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>\'s independence until an alternative to Jagan could be identified, supported, and brought into office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Worn down by the <a href="/wiki/First_Indochina_War" title="First Indochina War">communist guerrilla war for Vietnamese independence</a> and handed a watershed defeat by communist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viet_Minh" title="Viet Minh">Viet Minh</a> rebels at the 1954 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dien_Bien_Phu" title="Battle of Dien Bien Phu">Battle of Dien Bien Phu</a>, the French accepted a negotiated abandonment of their colonial stake in <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geneva_Conference_(1954)" title="Geneva Conference (1954)">Geneva Conference</a>, peace accords were signed, leaving Vietnam divided between a pro-Soviet administration in <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnam</a> and a pro-Western administration in <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a> at the <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_north" title="17th parallel north">17th parallel north</a>. Between 1954 and 1961, Eisenhower\'s United States sent economic aid and military advisers to strengthen South Vietnam\'s pro-Western regime against communist efforts to destabilize it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-8"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many emerging nations of Asia, Africa, and Latin America rejected the pressure to choose sides in the East-West competition. In 1955, at the <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Conference" title="Bandung Conference">Bandung Conference</a> in Indonesia, dozens of Third World governments resolved to stay out of the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The consensus reached at Bandung culminated with the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>-headquartered <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> in 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-6"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Khrushchev broadened Moscow\'s policy to establish ties with <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and other key neutral states. Independence movements in the Third World transformed the post-war order into a more pluralistic world of decolonized African and Middle Eastern nations and of rising nationalism in Asia and Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-9"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sino-Soviet_split">Sino-Soviet split</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg/290px-Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg/435px-Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg/580px-Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sino-Soviet_split_1980.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing the relations of the communist states after the Sino-Soviet split as of 1980: <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #dd0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The USSR and pro-Soviet communist states</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FCC200; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;China and pro-Chinese communist states</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Neutral communist nations (<a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #e0e0e0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non-communist states</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The period after 1956 was marked by serious setbacks for the Soviet Union, most notably the breakdown of the Sino-Soviet alliance, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a>. Mao had defended Stalin when Khrushchev criticized him in 1956, and treated the new Soviet leader as a superficial upstart, accusing him of having lost his revolutionary edge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis142_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis142-182">[182]</a></sup> For his part, Khrushchev, disturbed by Mao\'s glib attitude toward nuclear war, referred to the Chinese leader as a "lunatic on a throne".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After this, Khrushchev made many desperate attempts to reconstitute the Sino-Soviet alliance, but Mao considered it useless and denied any proposal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis142_182-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis142-182">[182]</a></sup> The Chinese-Soviet animosity spilled out in an intra-communist propaganda war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Further on, the Soviets focused on a bitter rivalry with Mao\'s China for leadership of the global communist movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Historian Lorenz M. L&#252;thi argues:\n</p>\n<dl><dd>The Sino-Soviet split was one of the key events of the Cold War, equal in importance to the construction of the Berlin Wall, the Cuban Missile Crisis, the Second Vietnam War, and <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations#Rapprochement" title="China&#8211;United States relations">Sino-American rapprochement</a>. The split helped to determine the framework of the Second Cold War in general, and influenced the course of the Second Vietnam War in particular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Space_Race">Space Race</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3967" data-file-width="3929" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg/180px-Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg/270px-Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg/360px-Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The United States <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">reached the moon</a> in 1969.</div></div></div>\n<p>On the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> front, the United States and the USSR pursued nuclear rearmament and developed long-range weapons with which they could strike the territory of the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byrd_47-6"><a href="#cite_note-Byrd-47">[47]</a></sup> In August 1957, the Soviets successfully launched the world\'s first <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile" title="Intercontinental ballistic missile">intercontinental ballistic missile</a> (ICBM),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> and in October they launched the first Earth satellite, <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik 1</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The launch of Sputnik inaugurated the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>. This culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo</a> <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">Moon landings</a>, which astronaut <a href="/wiki/Frank_Borman" title="Frank Borman">Frank Borman</a> later described as "just a battle in the Cold War."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuban_Revolution_and_the_Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion">Cuban Revolution and the Bay of Pigs Invasion</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion" title="Bay of Pigs Invasion">Bay of Pigs Invasion</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1197" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/170px-CheyFidel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/255px-CheyFidel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/CheyFidel.jpg/340px-CheyFidel.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CheyFidel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> (right) in 1961</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/26th_of_July_Movement" title="26th of July Movement">26th of July Movement</a>, led by young revolutionaries <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a>, seized power in the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> on 1 January 1959, toppling President <a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a>, whose unpopular regime had been denied arms by the Eisenhower administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Cuba&#8211;United States relations">Diplomatic relations between Cuba and the United States</a> continued for some time after Batista\'s fall, but President Eisenhower deliberately left the capital to avoid meeting Castro during the latter\'s trip to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington,_DC" title="Washington, DC">Washington, DC</a> in April, leaving Vice President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> to conduct the meeting in his place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Cuba began negotiating for arms purchases from the Eastern Bloc in March 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 1961, just prior to leaving office, Eisenhower formally severed relations with the Cuban government. In April 1961, the administration of newly elected American President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> mounted an unsuccessful CIA-organized <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion" title="Bay of Pigs Invasion">ship-borne invasion</a> of the island at Playa Gir&#243;n and Playa Larga in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_Province" title="Santa Clara Province">Santa Clara Province</a>&#8212;a failure that publicly humiliated the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_1998,_95_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_1998,_95-193">[193]</a></sup> Castro responded by publicly embracing <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism"
