title="Marxism&#8211;Leninism">Marxism&#8211;Leninism</a>, and the Soviet Union pledged to <a href="/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93Soviet_Union_relations" title="Cuba&#8211;Soviet Union relations">provide further support</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith_1998,_95_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-Smith_1998,_95-193">[193]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Berlin_Crisis_of_1961">Berlin Crisis of 1961</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Crisis_of_1961" title="Berlin Crisis of 1961">Berlin Crisis of 1961</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_emigration_and_defection" title="Eastern Bloc emigration and defection">Eastern Bloc emigration and defection</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks,_Berlin_1961.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1507" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg/220px-US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg/330px-US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg/440px-US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks%2C_Berlin_1961.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_tanks_face_off_against_Soviet_tanks,_Berlin_1961.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tanks_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Tanks in the Soviet Union">Soviet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanks_of_the_United_States" title="Tanks of the United States">American tanks</a> face each other at <a href="/wiki/Checkpoint_Charlie" title="Checkpoint Charlie">Checkpoint Charlie</a> during the Berlin Crisis of 1961.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Crisis_of_1961" title="Berlin Crisis of 1961">Berlin Crisis of 1961</a> was the last major incident in the Cold War regarding the status of Berlin and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Germany_(1945%E2%80%9390)" title="History of Germany (1945&#8211;90)">post&#8211;World War II Germany</a>. By the early 1950s, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_emigration_and_defection" title="Eastern Bloc emigration and defection">Soviet approach to restricting emigration movement</a> was emulated by most of the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dowty114_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-dowty114-194">[194]</a></sup> However, hundreds of thousands of <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germans</a> annually emigrated to <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> through a "loophole" in the system that existed between <a href="/wiki/East_Berlin" title="East Berlin">East Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a>, where the four occupying World War II powers governed movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harrison99_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-harrison99-195">[195]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The emigration resulted in a massive "<a href="/wiki/Human_capital_flight" title="Human capital flight">brain drain</a>" from East Germany to West Germany of younger educated professionals, such that nearly 20% of East Germany\'s population had migrated to West Germany by 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dowty122_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-dowty122-196">[196]</a></sup> That June, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> issued a new <a href="/wiki/Ultimatum" title="Ultimatum">ultimatum</a> demanding the withdrawal of <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied forces</a> from West Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> The request was rebuffed, and on 13 August, East Germany erected a barbed-wire barrier that would eventually be expanded through construction into the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>, effectively closing the loophole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pearson75_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-pearson75-198">[198]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Cuban_Missile_Crisis_and_Khrushchev.27s_ouster"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuban_Missile_Crisis_and_Khrushchev\'s_ouster">Cuban Missile Crisis and Khrushchev\'s ouster</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Project" title="Cuban Project">Cuban Project</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_missiles.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1121" data-file-width="1160" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Cuban_missiles.jpg/220px-Cuban_missiles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Cuban_missiles.jpg/330px-Cuban_missiles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Cuban_missiles.jpg/440px-Cuban_missiles.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_missiles.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial photograph of a Soviet missile site in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, taken by a US <a href="/wiki/Surveillance_aircraft" title="Surveillance aircraft">spy aircraft</a>, 1 November 1962</div></div></div>\n<p>The Kennedy administration continued seeking ways to oust Castro following the Bay of Pigs Invasion, experimenting with various ways of covertly facilitating the overthrow of the Cuban government. Significant hopes were pinned on a covert program named the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Project" title="Cuban Project">Cuban Project</a>, devised under the Kennedy administration in 1961. Khrushchev learned of the project in February 1962,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zubok_1994,_158-159_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zubok_1994,_158-159-199">[199]</a></sup> and preparations to install Soviet nuclear missiles in Cuba were undertaken in response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zubok_1994,_158-159_199-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zubok_1994,_158-159-199">[199]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Alarmed, Kennedy considered various reactions. He ultimately responded to the installation of nuclear missiles in Cuba with a naval blockade, and he presented an ultimatum to the Soviets. Khrushchev backed down from a confrontation, and the Soviet Union removed the missiles in return for an American pledge not to invade Cuba again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> Castro later admitted that "I would have agreed to the use of nuclear weapons. ... we took it for granted that it would become a nuclear war anyway, and that we were going to disappear."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> (October&#8211;November 1962) brought the world closer to <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">nuclear war</a> than ever before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The aftermath of the crisis led to the first efforts in the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_arms_race" title="Nuclear arms race">nuclear arms race</a> at nuclear disarmament and improving relations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palmowski_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-Palmowski-148">[148]</a></sup> although the Cold War\'s first arms control agreement, the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System" title="Antarctic Treaty System">Antarctic Treaty</a>, had come into force in 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1964, Khrushchev\'s Kremlin colleagues managed to <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev#Removal" title="Nikita Khrushchev">oust</a> him, but allowed him a peaceful retirement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis119_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis119-204">[204]</a></sup> Accused of rudeness and incompetence, he was also credited with ruining Soviet agriculture and bringing the world to the <a href="/wiki/Brinkmanship#Cold_War" title="Brinkmanship">brink of nuclear war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis119_204-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis119-204">[204]</a></sup> Khrushchev had become an international embarrassment when he authorized construction of the Berlin Wall, a public humiliation for Marxism&#8211;Leninism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis119_204-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis119-204">[204]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Confrontation_through_d.C3.A9tente_.281962.E2.80.931979.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Confrontation_through_d&#233;tente_(1962&#8211;1979)">Confrontation through d&#233;tente (1962&#8211;1979)</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_(1962%E2%80%931979)" title="Cold War (1962&#8211;1979)">Cold War (1962&#8211;1979)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="689" data-file-width="655" decoding="async" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/220px-1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/330px-1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg/440px-1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1973_NATO_and_WP_troop_strengths_in_Europe.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NATO and Warsaw Pact troop strengths in Europe in 1973</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1802" data-file-width="2962" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg/220px-F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg/330px-F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg/440px-F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F-4B_VF-151_CV-41_TU-95.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>United States Navy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-4_Phantom_II" title="F-4 Phantom II">F-4 Phantom II</a> intercepts a Soviet <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-95" title="Tupolev Tu-95">Tupolev Tu-95</a> D aircraft in the early 1970s.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the course of the 1960s and 1970s, Cold War participants struggled to adjust to a new, more complicated pattern of international relations in which the world was no longer divided into two clearly opposed blocs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-7"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup> From the beginning of the post-war period, Western Europe and Japan rapidly recovered from the destruction of World War II and sustained strong economic growth through the 1950s and 1960s, with per capita GDPs approaching those of the United States, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_economies" title="Eastern Bloc economies">Eastern Bloc economies stagnated</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-8"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardt16_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-hardt16-205">[205]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>, Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries (<a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>) cut their petroleum output. This raised oil prices and hurt Western economies, but helped Russia by generating a huge flow of money from its oil sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the oil crisis, combined with the growing influence of Third World alignments such as OPEC and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, less powerful countries had more room to assert their independence and often showed themselves resistant to pressure from either superpower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._212_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._212-132">[132]</a></sup> Meanwhile, Moscow was forced to turn its attention inward to deal with the Soviet Union\'s deep-seated domestic economic problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-9"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup> During this period, Soviet leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Kosygin" title="Alexei Kosygin">Alexei Kosygin</a> embraced the notion of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="D&#233;tente">d&#233;tente</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-10"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_withdrawal_from_NATO">French withdrawal from NATO</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/NATO#French_withdrawal" title="NATO">NATO &#167;&#160;French withdrawal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Foreign policy of Charles de Gaulle">Foreign policy of Charles de Gaulle</a></div>\n<p>The unity of NATO was breached early in its history, with a crisis occurring during <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>\'s presidency of France. De Gaulle protested at the strong role of the United States in the organization and what he perceived as a <a href="/wiki/Special_Relationship" title="Special Relationship">special relationship</a> between the United States and the United Kingdom. In a memorandum sent to President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a> on 17 September 1958, he argued for the creation of a tripartite directorate that would put France on an equal footing with the United States and the United Kingdom, and also for the expansion of NATO\'s coverage to include geographical areas of interest to France, most notably <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">French Algeria</a>, where France was waging a counter-insurgency and sought NATO assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deGuaulle_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-deGuaulle-207">[207]</a></sup> De Gaulle considered the response he received to be unsatisfactory, and began the development of an <a href="/wiki/Force_de_dissuasion" title="Force de dissuasion">independent French nuclear deterrent</a>. In 1966 he withdrew France from NATO\'s military structures and expelled NATO troops from French soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia">Invasion of Czechoslovakia</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">Prague Spring</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2720" data-file-width="4048" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg/220px-10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg/330px-10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg/440px-10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:10_Soviet_Invasion_of_Czechoslovakia_-_Flickr_-_The_Central_Intelligence_Agency.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">invasion of Czechoslovakia</a> by the Soviet Union in 1968 was one of the biggest military operations on European soil since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1968, a period of political liberalization took place in <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic" title="Czechoslovak Socialist Republic">Czechoslovakia</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">Prague Spring</a>. An "<a href="/wiki/Action_Programme_(1968)" title="Action Programme (1968)">Action Program</a>" of reforms included increasing <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement" title="Freedom of movement">freedom of movement</a>, along with an economic emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Final_good" title="Final good">consumer goods</a>, the possibility of a multiparty government, limitations on the power of the secret police,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> and potential withdrawal from the Warsaw Pact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._150_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._150-211">[211]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In answer to the Prague Spring, on 20 August 1968, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Army" title="Soviet Army">Soviet Army</a>, together with most of their Warsaw Pact allies, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">invaded Czechoslovakia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> The invasion was followed by a wave of emigration, including an estimated 70,000 Czechs and Slovaks initially fleeing, with the total eventually reaching 300,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> The invasion sparked intense protests from Yugoslavia, Romania, China, and from Western European communist parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._154_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._154-214">[214]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brezhnev_Doctrine">Brezhnev Doctrine</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brezhnev_Doctrine" title="Brezhnev Doctrine">Brezhnev Doctrine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1998" data-file-width="2944" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png/220px-Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png/330px-Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png/440px-Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leonid_Brezhnev_and_Richard_Nixon_talks_in_1973.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> in Washington, 1973; this was a high-water mark in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="D&#233;tente">d&#233;tente</a> between the USSR and the US.</div></div></div>\n<p>In September 1968, during a speech at the Fifth Congress of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_United_Workers%27_Party" title="Polish United Workers\' Party">Polish United Workers\' Party</a> one month after the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">invasion of Czechoslovakia</a>, Brezhnev outlined the <a href="/wiki/Brezhnev_Doctrine" title="Brezhnev Doctrine">Brezhnev Doctrine</a>, in which he claimed the right to violate the sovereignty of any country attempting to replace Marxism&#8211;Leninism with capitalism. During the speech, Brezhnev stated:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._150_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._150-211">[211]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>When forces that are hostile to socialism try to turn the development of some socialist country towards capitalism, it becomes not only a problem of the country concerned, but a common problem and concern of all socialist countries.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>The doctrine found its origins in the failures of Marxism&#8211;Leninism in states like Poland, Hungary and East Germany, which were facing a declining standard of living contrasting with the prosperity of West Germany and the rest of Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_World_escalations">Third World escalations</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Civil_War" title="Dominican Civil War">Dominican Civil War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_mass_killings_of_1965%E2%80%9366" title="Indonesian mass killings of 1965&#8211;66">Indonesian mass killings of 1965&#8211;66</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, <a href="/wiki/1973_Chilean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1973 Chilean coup d\'&#233;tat">1973 Chilean coup d\'&#233;tat</a>, <a href="/wiki/1973_Uruguayan_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1973 Uruguayan coup d\'&#233;tat">1973 Uruguayan coup d\'&#233;tat</a>, <a href="/wiki/1976_Argentine_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1976 Argentine coup d\'&#233;tat">1976 Argentine coup d\'&#233;tat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation Condor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Task_Force_74" title="Task Force 74">Task Force 74</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_of_Attrition" title="War of Attrition">War of Attrition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">Yom Kippur War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ogaden_War" title="Ogaden War">Ogaden War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_African_Border_War" title="South African Border War">South African Border War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_invasion_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian invasion of East Timor">Indonesian invasion of East Timor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Re-education_camp_(Vietnam)" title="Re-education camp (Vietnam)">Re-education camp (Vietnam)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_boat_people" title="Vietnamese boat people">Vietnamese boat people</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stability%E2%80%93instability_paradox" title="Stability&#8211;instability paradox">Stability&#8211;instability paradox</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:178px;"><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:176px"><video class="kskin" controls="" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Speech on the Vietnam War given by President Lyndon B. Johnson on 29 September 1967</div></div></div>\n<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Presidency of Lyndon B. Johnson">Administration</a>, which gained power after the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination of John F. Kennedy</a>, the U.S. took a more hardline stance on Latin America&#8212;sometimes called the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mann_Doctrine" title="Mann Doctrine">Mann Doctrine</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeberGoodNeighbor_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeberGoodNeighbor-216">[216]</a></sup> In 1964, the Brazilian military <a href="/wiki/1964_Brazilian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1964 Brazilian coup d\'&#233;tat">overthrew the government</a> of president <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Goulart" title="Jo&#227;o Goulart">Jo&#227;o Goulart</a> with U.S. backing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeberGoodNeighbor_216-1"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeberGoodNeighbor-216">[216]</a></sup> In late April 1965, the U.S. sent some 22,000 troops to the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> for a one-year occupation in an invasion codenamed <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Civil_War" title="Dominican Civil War">Operation Power Pack</a>, citing the threat of the emergence of a Cuban-style revolution in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-10"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Garc%C3%ADa-Godoy" title="H&#233;ctor Garc&#237;a-Godoy">H&#233;ctor Garc&#237;a-Godoy</a> acted as provisional president, until conservative former president <a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Balaguer" title="Joaqu&#237;n Balaguer">Joaqu&#237;n Balaguer</a> won the 1966 presidential election against non-campaigning former President <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bosch_(politician)" title="Juan Bosch (politician)">Juan Bosch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzigsohn_2000,_41-42_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Itzigsohn_2000,_41-42-217">[217]</a></sup> Activists for Bosch\'s <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Revolutionary_Party" title="Dominican Revolutionary Party">Dominican Revolutionary Party</a> were violently harassed by the Dominican police and armed forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzigsohn_2000,_41-42_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Itzigsohn_2000,_41-42-217">[217]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="557" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg/220px-Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg/330px-Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg/440px-Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bruce_Crandall%27s_UH-1D.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. combat operations during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ia_Drang" title="Battle of Ia Drang">Battle of Ia Drang</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a>, November 1965</div></div></div>\n<p>In Indonesia, the hardline anti-communist <a href="/wiki/Suharto" title="Suharto">General Suharto</a> wrested control of the state from his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a> in an attempt to <a href="/wiki/Transition_to_the_New_Order" title="Transition to the New Order">establish a "New Order"</a>. From 1965 to 1966, with the <a href="/wiki/CIA_activities_in_Indonesia#Anti-communist_purge" title="CIA activities in Indonesia">aid of the United States</a> and other Western governments,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atlantic2017_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atlantic2017-222">[222]</a></sup> the military <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_mass_killings_of_1965%E2%80%9366" title="Indonesian mass killings of 1965&#8211;66">led the mass killing</a> of more than 500,000 members and sympathizers of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Indonesia" title="Communist Party of Indonesia">Indonesian Communist Party</a> and other leftist organizations, and detained hundreds of thousands more in prison camps around the country under extremely inhumane conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> A top-secret CIA report stated that the massacres "rank as one of the worst <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murders</a> of the 20th century, along with the Soviet purges of the 1930s, the Nazi mass murders during the Second World War, and the Maoist bloodbath of the early 1950s."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blumenthal_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blumenthal-225">[225]</a></sup> These killings served U.S. strategic interests and constitute a major turning point in the Cold War as the balance of power shifted in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atlantic2017_222-1"><a href="#cite_note-Atlantic2017-222">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_warfare_in_South_Vietnam,_1963%E2%80%9369" title="Joint warfare in South Vietnam, 1963&#8211;69">Escalating the scale of American intervention</a> in the ongoing conflict between <a href="/wiki/Ngo_Dinh_Diem" title="Ngo Dinh Diem">Ng&#244; &#272;&#236;nh Di&#7879;m</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnamese</a> government and the communist <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">National Front for the Liberation of South Vietnam</a> (NLF) insurgents opposing it, Johnson deployed some 575,000 troops in Southeast Asia to defeat the NLF and their North Vietnamese allies in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, but his costly policy weakened the US economy and, by 1975, it ultimately culminated in what most of the world saw as a humiliating defeat of the world\'s most powerful superpower at the hands of one of the world\'s poorest nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-11"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="468" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg/220px-Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg/330px-Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg/440px-Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reuni%C3%B3n_Pinochet_-_Kissinger.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chilean leader <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a> shaking hands with Henry Kissinger in 1976</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Chile" title="Socialist Party of Chile">Socialist Party</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Allende" title="Salvador Allende">Salvador Allende</a> won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chilean_presidential_election,_1970" title="Chilean presidential election, 1970">presidential election of 1970</a>, becoming the first democratically elected <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a> to become president of a country in the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Allende_Profile_2003_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Allende_Profile_2003-227">[227]</a></sup> The CIA targeted Allende for removal and operated to undermine his support domestically, which contributed to a period of unrest culminating in General <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/1973_Chilean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1973 Chilean coup d\'&#233;tat">coup d\'&#233;tat</a> on 11 September 1973. Pinochet consolidated power as a military dictator, Allende\'s reforms of the economy were rolled back, and leftist opponents were killed or detained in internment camps under the <a href="/wiki/Direcci%C3%B3n_de_Inteligencia_Nacional" title="Direcci&#243;n de Inteligencia Nacional">Direcci&#243;n de Inteligencia Nacional</a> (DINA). The Pinochet regime would go on to be one of the leading participants in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Condor" title="Operation Condor">Operation <i>Condor</i></a>, an international campaign of political assassination and <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">state terrorism</a> organized by right-wing military dictatorships in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a> of South America that was covertly supported by the US government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1973" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Secretary_of_State_Henry_A._Kissinger_Using_the_Telephone_in_Deputy_National_Security_Advisor_Brent..._-_NARA_-_186804.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">Henry Kissinger</a>, who was <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Advisor_(United_States)" title="National Security Advisor (United States)">US National Security Advisor</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> under Presidents Nixon and Ford, was a central figure in the Cold War while in office (1969&#8211;1977).</div></div></div>\n<p>The Middle East remained a source of contention. Egypt, which received the bulk of its arms and economic assistance from the USSR, was a troublesome client, with a reluctant Soviet Union feeling obliged to assist in both the 1967 <a href="/wiki/Six-Day_War" title="Six-Day War">Six-Day War</a> (with advisers and technicians) and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Attrition" title="War of Attrition">War of Attrition</a> (with pilots and aircraft) against pro-Western Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> Despite the beginning of an Egyptian shift from a pro-Soviet to a pro-American orientation in 1972 (under Egypt\'s new leader <a href="/wiki/Anwar_Sadat" title="Anwar Sadat">Anwar Sadat</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grenville_&amp;_Wasserstein_1987,_701_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grenville_&amp;_Wasserstein_1987,_701-232">[232]</a></sup> rumors of imminent Soviet intervention on the Egyptians\' behalf during the 1973 <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">Yom Kippur War</a> brought about a massive American mobilization that threatened to wreck d&#233;tente.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Although pre-Sadat Egypt had been the largest recipient of Soviet aid in the Middle East, the Soviets were also successful in establishing close relations with communist <a href="/wiki/South_Yemen" title="South Yemen">South Yemen</a>, as well as the nationalist governments of <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grenville_&amp;_Wasserstein_1987,_701_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-Grenville_&amp;_Wasserstein_1987,_701-232">[232]</a></sup> Iraq signed a 15-year Treaty of Friendship and Cooperation with the Soviet Union in 1972. According to historian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_R.H._Tripp" title="Charles R.H. Tripp">Charles R.H. Tripp</a>, the treaty upset "the U.S.-sponsored security system established as part of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Cold_War" title="Arab Cold War">Cold War in the Middle East</a>. It appeared that any enemy of the Baghdad regime was a potential ally of the United States."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tripp_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tripp-234">[234]</a></sup> In response, the U.S. covertly financed Kurdish rebels led by <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Barzani" title="Mustafa Barzani">Mustafa Barzani</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Iraqi%E2%80%93Kurdish_War" title="Second Iraqi&#8211;Kurdish War">Second Iraqi&#8211;Kurdish War</a>; the Kurds were defeated in 1975, leading to the forcible relocation of hundreds of thousands of Kurdish civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tripp_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tripp-234">[234]</a></sup> Indirect Soviet assistance to the Palestinian side of the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli&#8211;Palestinian conflict">Israeli&#8211;Palestinian conflict</a> included support for <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a> (PLO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In East Africa, a territorial dispute between <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Ogaden" title="Ogaden">Ogaden</a> region resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Ogaden_War" title="Ogaden War">Ogaden War</a>. Around June 1977, Somali troops occupied the Ogaden and began advancing inland towards Ethiopian positions in the <a href="/wiki/Ahmar_Mountains" title="Ahmar Mountains">Ahmar Mountains</a>. Both countries were client states of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>; Somalia was led by self-proclaimed Marxist military leader <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Siad Barre</a>, and Ethiopia was controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Derg" title="Derg">Derg</a>, a cabal of military generals loyal to the pro-Soviet <a href="/wiki/Mengistu_Haile_Mariam" title="Mengistu Haile Mariam">Mengistu Haile Mariam</a>, who had declared the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Republic_of_Ethiopia" title="People\'s Democratic Republic of Ethiopia">People\'s Democratic Republic of Ethiopia</a> in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Erlich_2008,_84-86_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-Erlich_2008,_84-86-236">[236]</a></sup> The Soviets initially attempted to exert a moderating influence on both states, but in November 1977 Barre broke off relations with Moscow and expelled his Soviet military advisers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perrett_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perrett-237">[237]</a></sup> He then turned to the <a href="/wiki/Safari_Club" title="Safari Club">Safari Club</a>&#8212;a group of pro-American intelligence agencies including those of Iran, Egypt, and Saudi Arabia&#8212;for support and weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> While declining to take a direct part in hostilities, the Soviet Union did provide the impetuous for a successful Ethiopian counteroffensive to expel Somalia from the Ogaden. The counteroffensive was planned at the command level by Soviet advisers attached to the Ethiopian general staff, and bolstered by the delivery of millions of dollars\' of sophisticated Soviet arms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perrett_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-Perrett-237">[237]</a></sup> About 11,000 Cuban troops spearheaded the primary effort, after receiving a hasty training on some of the newly delivered Soviet weapons systems by East German instructors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perrett_237-2"><a href="#cite_note-Perrett-237">[237]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="579" data-file-width="616" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/220px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/330px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/440px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cuban tank in the streets of <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, 1976</div></div></div>\n<p>On 24 April 1974, the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> ousted <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Caetano" title="Marcelo Caetano">Marcelo Caetano</a> and Portugal\'s right-wing <i><a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a></i> government, sounding the death knell for the Portuguese Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Days_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-Days-240">[240]</a></sup> Independence was hastily granted to a number of Portuguese colonies, including <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, where the disintegration of colonial rule was followed by a violent civil war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stockwell_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stockwell-241">[241]</a></sup> There were three rival militant factions competing for power in Angola, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" title="People\'s Movement for the Liberation of Angola">People\'s Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a> (MPLA), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Union_for_the_Total_Independence_of_Angola" title="National Union for the Total Independence of Angola">National Union for the Total Independence of Angola</a> (UNITA), and the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_of_Angola" title="National Liberation Front of Angola">National Liberation Front of Angola</a> (FNLA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-242">[242]</a></sup> While all three possessed vaguely socialist leanings, the MPLA was the only party which enjoyed close ties to the Soviet Union and was openly committed to Marxist policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_242-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-242">[242]</a></sup> Its adherence to the concept of a one-party state alienated it from the FNLA and UNITA, which began portraying themselves as anti-communist and pro-Western in orientation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_242-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-242">[242]</a></sup> When the Soviets began supplying the MPLA with arms, the CIA offered substantial covert aid to the FNLA and UNITA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-243">[243]</a></sup> The MPLA eventually requested direct military support from Moscow in the form of ground troops, but the Soviets declined, offering to send advisers but no combat personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_243-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-243">[243]</a></sup> Cuba was more forthcoming and began amassing troops in Angola to assist the MPLA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_243-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-243">[243]</a></sup> By November 1975 there were over a thousand Cuban soldiers in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_243-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-243">[243]</a></sup> The persistent buildup of Cuban troops and Soviet weapons allowed the MPLA to secure victory and blunt an abortive intervention by Zairean and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> troops, which had deployed in a belated attempt to assist the FNLA and UNITA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-244">[244]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1168" data-file-width="1760" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg/220px-Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg/330px-Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg/440px-Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skulls_from_the_killing_fields.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Kampuchea" title="Democratic Kampuchea">regime</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a>, one to three million people died due to the policies of his four-year premiership.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the Vietnam War, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Sihanouk" title="Prince Sihanouk">Prince Sihanouk</a> of Cambodia welcomed North Vietnam to <a href="/wiki/Sihanouk_Trail" title="Sihanouk Trail">use border areas of his country as military bases</a>. American and South Vietnamese forces responded to these actions with a brief <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Campaign" title="Cambodian Campaign">ground incursion</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Operation_Menu" title="Operation Menu">bombing campaign</a>, which contributed to the violence of the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Civil_War" title="Cambodian Civil War">Cambodian Civil War</a> between the American-backed government of <a href="/wiki/Lon_Nol" title="Lon Nol">Lon Nol</a> and communist <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> insurgents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> Documents uncovered from the Soviet archives reveal that the North Vietnamese invasion of Cambodia in 1970 was launched at the request of the Khmer Rouge after negotiations with <a href="/wiki/Nuon_Chea" title="Nuon Chea">Nuon Chea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> US carpet bombing <a href="/wiki/Operation_Freedom_Deal" title="Operation Freedom Deal">lasted until 1973</a>, and while it prevented the Khmer Rouge from seizing the capital, it also accelerated the collapse of rural society, increased social polarization,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> and killed tens of thousands of civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After taking power and distancing himself from the Vietnamese,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> Khmer Rouge leader <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a> killed 1&#8211;3 million Cambodians in the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge_Killing_Fields" title="Khmer Rouge Killing Fields">killing fields</a>, out of a 1975 population of roughly 8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heuveline,_Patrick_2001_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heuveline,_Patrick_2001-250">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marek_Sliwinski_1995_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marek_Sliwinski_1995-251">[251]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banister,_Judith_1993_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Banister,_Judith_1993-252">[252]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Martin_Shaw_(sociologist)" title="Martin Shaw (sociologist)">Martin Shaw</a> described these atrocities as "the purest genocide of the Cold War era."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> Backed by the <a href="/wiki/Kampuchean_United_Front_for_National_Salvation" title="Kampuchean United Front for National Salvation">Kampuchean United Front for National Salvation</a>, an organization of Khmer pro-Soviet Communists and Khmer Rouge defectors led by <a href="/wiki/Heng_Samrin" title="Heng Samrin">Heng Samrin</a>, Vietnam invaded Cambodia on 22 December 1978. The <a href="/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Vietnamese_War" title="Cambodian&#8211;Vietnamese War">invasion succeeded</a> in deposing Pol Pot, but the new state would struggle to gain international recognition beyond the Soviet Bloc sphere, despite the previous international outcry at the Pol Pot regime\'s gross human rights violations, and it would become bogged down in a guerrilla war led from refugee camps located on the border with <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>. Following the destruction of Khmer Rouge, the national reconstruction of Cambodia would be severely hampered, and Vietnam would suffer a punitive <a href="/wiki/Sino-Vietnamese_War" title="Sino-Vietnamese War">Chinese attack</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSloc_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSloc-254">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hu-huong_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-hu-huong-255">[255]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sino-American_rapprochement">Sino-American rapprochement</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1972_Nixon_visit_to_China" title="1972 Nixon visit to China">1972 Nixon visit to China</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader,_Mao_Tse-_Tung,_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2334" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader%2C_Mao_Tse-_Tung%2C_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif/lossy-page1-220px-President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader%2C_Mao_Tse-_Tung%2C_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader%2C_Mao_Tse-_Tung%2C_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif/lossy-page1-330px-President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader%2C_Mao_Tse-_Tung%2C_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader%2C_Mao_Tse-_Tung%2C_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif/lossy-page1-440px-President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader%2C_Mao_Tse-_Tung%2C_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Nixon_meets_with_China%27s_Communist_Party_Leader,_Mao_Tse-_Tung,_02-29-1972_-_NARA_-_194759.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> and US President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, during his visit in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a></div></div></div>\n<p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a>, tensions along the Chinese&#8211;Soviet border <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_border_conflict" title="Sino-Soviet border conflict">reached their peak</a> in 1969, and United States President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> decided to use the conflict to shift the balance of power towards the West in the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> The Chinese had sought improved relations with the Americans in order to gain advantage over the Soviets as well.\n</p><p>In February 1972, Nixon achieved a stunning rapprochement with China,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> traveling to Beijing and meeting with <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a>. At this time, the USSR achieved rough nuclear parity with the United States; meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> both weakened America\'s influence in the Third World and cooled relations with Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> Although indirect conflict between Cold War powers continued through the late 1960s and early 1970s, tensions were beginning to ease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palmowski_148-2"><a href="#cite_note-Palmowski-148">[148]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Nixon.2C_Brezhnev.2C_and_d.C3.A9tente"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Nixon,_Brezhnev,_and_d&#233;tente">Nixon, Brezhnev, and d&#233;tente</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Arms_Limitation_Talks" title="Strategic Arms Limitation Talks">Strategic Arms Limitation Talks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok_Summit_Meeting_on_Arms_Control" title="Vladivostok Summit Meeting on Arms Control">Vladivostok Summit Meeting on Arms Control</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Accords" title="Helsinki Accords">Helsinki Accords</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="630" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg/220px-Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg/330px-Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg/440px-Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carter_Brezhnev_sign_SALT_II.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> sign the SALT II treaty, 18 June 1979, in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Following his visit to China, Nixon met with Soviet leaders, including Brezhnev in Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-nb_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-nb-259">[259]</a></sup> These <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Arms_Limitation_Talks" title="Strategic Arms Limitation Talks">Strategic Arms Limitation Talks</a> resulted in two landmark arms control treaties: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SALT_I" title="SALT I">SALT I</a>, the first comprehensive limitation pact signed by the two superpowers, and the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Ballistic_Missile_Treaty" title="Anti-Ballistic Missile Treaty">Anti-Ballistic Missile Treaty</a>, which banned the development of systems designed to intercept incoming missiles. These aimed to limit the development of costly anti-ballistic missiles and nuclear missiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karabell_91-11"><a href="#cite_note-Karabell-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nixon and Brezhnev proclaimed a new era of "peaceful coexistence" and established the groundbreaking new policy of <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="D&#233;tente">d&#233;tente</a></i> (or cooperation) between the two superpowers. Meanwhile, Brezhnev attempted to revive the Soviet economy, which was declining in part because of heavy military expenditures. Between 1972 and 1974, the two sides also agreed to strengthen their economic ties,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-12"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup> including agreements for increased trade. As a result of their meetings, <i>d&#233;tente</i> would replace the hostility of the Cold War and the two countries would live mutually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup>\n</p><p>These developments coincided with the "<a href="/wiki/Ostpolitik" title="Ostpolitik">Ostpolitik</a>" policy of West German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._154_214-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._154-214">[214]</a></sup> an effort to normalize relations between West Germany and Eastern Europe. Other agreements were concluded to stabilize the situation in Europe, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Accords" title="Helsinki Accords">Helsinki Accords</a> signed at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conference_on_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Conference on Security and Co-operation in Europe">Conference on Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="711" data-file-width="496" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg/220px-1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg/330px-1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg/440px-1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1979_Iranian_Revolution.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iranian people protesting against the <a href="/wiki/Pahlavi_dynasty" title="Pahlavi dynasty">Pahlavi dynasty</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Iranian Revolution</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Kissinger and Nixon were "realists" who deemphasized idealistic goals like anti-communism or promotion of democracy worldwide, because those goals were too expensive in terms of America\'s economic capabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> Instead of a Cold War they wanted peace, trade and cultural exchanges. They realized that Americans were no longer willing to tax themselves for idealistic foreign policy goals, especially for containment policies that never seemed to produce positive results. Instead Nixon and Kissinger sought to downsize America\'s global commitments in proportion to its reduced economic, moral and political power. They rejected "idealism" as impractical and too expensive, and neither man showed much sensitivity to the plight of people living under Communism. Kissinger\'s realism fell out of fashion as idealism returned to American foreign policy with Carter\'s moralism emphasizing human rights, and Reagan\'s rollback strategy aimed at destroying Communism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_1970s_deterioration_of_relations">Late 1970s deterioration of relations</span></h3>\n<p>In the 1970s, the KGB, led by <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Andropov" title="Yuri Andropov">Yuri Andropov</a>, continued to persecute distinguished Soviet personalities such as <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Solzhenitsyn" title="Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn">Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Sakharov" title="Andrei Sakharov">Andrei Sakharov</a>, who were criticising the Soviet leadership in harsh terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> Indirect conflict between the superpowers continued through this period of d&#233;tente in the Third World, particularly during political crises in the Middle East, Chile, Ethiopia, and Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although President <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> tried to place another limit on the arms race with a <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Arms_Limitation_Talks" title="Strategic Arms Limitation Talks">SALT II</a> agreement in 1979,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> his efforts were undermined by the other events that year, including the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Iranian Revolution</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">Nicaraguan Revolution</a>, which both ousted pro-US regimes, and his retaliation against Soviet intervention in Afghanistan in December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafeber_1993_81-13"><a href="#cite_note-Lafeber_1993-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id=".22Second_Cold_War.22_.281979.E2.80.931985.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id=\'"Second_Cold_War"_(1979&#8211;1985)\'>"Second Cold War" (1979&#8211;1985)</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_(1979%E2%80%931985)" title="Cold War (1979&#8211;1985)">Cold War (1979&#8211;1985)</a></div>\n<p>The term <i>second Cold War</i> refers to the period of intensive reawakening of Cold War tensions and conflicts in the late 1970s and early 1980s. Tensions greatly increased between the major powers with both sides becoming more militaristic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-267">[267]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Patrick_Diggins" title="John Patrick Diggins">Diggins</a> says, "Reagan went all out to fight the second cold war, by supporting counterinsurgencies in the third world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cox_(academic)" title="Michael Cox (academic)">Cox</a> says, "The intensity of this \'second\' Cold War was as great as its duration was short."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_War_in_Afghanistan">Soviet War in Afghanistan</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(1978%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (1978&#8211;present)">War in Afghanistan (1978&#8211;present)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet&#8211;Afghan War">Soviet&#8211;Afghan War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1911" data-file-width="2707" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg/220px-Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg/330px-Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg/440px-Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reagan_sitting_with_people_from_the_Afghanistan-Pakistan_region_in_February_1983.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Reagan publicizes his support by meeting with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afghan_Mujahideen" title="Afghan Mujahideen">Afghan Mujahideen</a> leaders in the White House, 1983.</div></div></div>\n<p>In April 1978, the communist <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Party_of_Afghanistan" title="People\'s Democratic Party of Afghanistan">People\'s Democratic Party of Afghanistan</a> (PDPA) seized power in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Saur_Revolution" title="Saur Revolution">Saur Revolution</a>. Within months, opponents of the communist government launched an uprising in eastern Afghanistan that quickly expanded into a <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(1978%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (1978&#8211;present)">civil war</a> waged by guerrilla <a href="/wiki/Mujahideen" title="Mujahideen">mujahideen</a> against government forces countrywide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hussain_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-hussain-270">[270]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Unity_of_Afghanistan_Mujahideen" title="Islamic Unity of Afghanistan Mujahideen">Islamic Unity of Afghanistan Mujahideen</a> insurgents received military training and weapons in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warren_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-Warren-272">[272]</a></sup> while the Soviet Union sent thousands of military advisers to support the PDPA government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hussain_270-1"><a href="#cite_note-hussain-270">[270]</a></sup> Meanwhile, increasing friction between the competing factions of the PDPA&#8212;the dominant <a href="/wiki/Khalq" title="Khalq">Khalq</a> and the more moderate <a href="/wiki/Parcham" title="Parcham">Parcham</a>&#8212;resulted in the dismissal of Parchami cabinet members and the arrest of Parchami military officers under the pretext of a Parchami coup. By mid-1979, the United States had started a covert program to assist the mujahideen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 1979, Khalqist President <a href="/wiki/Nur_Muhammad_Taraki" title="Nur Muhammad Taraki">Nur Muhammad Taraki</a> was assassinated in a coup within the PDPA orchestrated by fellow Khalq member <a href="/wiki/Hafizullah_Amin" title="Hafizullah Amin">Hafizullah Amin</a>, who assumed the presidency. Distrusted by the Soviets, Amin was assassinated by Soviet special forces in December 1979. A Soviet-organized government, led by Parcham\'s <a href="/wiki/Babrak_Karmal" title="Babrak Karmal">Babrak Karmal</a> but inclusive of both factions, filled the vacuum. Soviet troops were deployed to stabilize Afghanistan under Karmal in more substantial numbers, although the Soviet government did not expect to do most of the fighting in Afghanistan. As a result, however, the Soviets were now directly involved in what had been a domestic war in Afghanistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Carter responded to the Soviet intervention by withdrawing the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Arms_Limitation_Talks" title="Strategic Arms Limitation Talks">SALT II</a> treaty from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senate</a>, imposing embargoes on grain and technology shipments to the USSR, and demanding a significant increase in military spending, and further announced that the United States would <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics_boycott" title="1980 Summer Olympics boycott">boycott</a> the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>. He described the Soviet incursion as "the most serious threat to the peace since the Second World War".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reagan_and_Thatcher">Reagan and Thatcher</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Reagan_Doctrine" title="Reagan Doctrine">Reagan Doctrine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thatcherism" title="Thatcherism">Thatcherism</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg"><img alt="Thatcher is the only woman in a room, where a dozen men in suits sit around an oval table. Regan and Thatcher sit opposite each other in the middle of the long axis of the table. The room is which is decorated in white, with drapes, a gold chandelier and a portrait of Lincoln." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="2033" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg/220px-Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg/330px-Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg/440px-Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reagan-Thatcher_cabinet_talks.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thatcher\'s Ministry meets with Reagan\'s Cabinet at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>, 1981.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_Map_1980.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="477" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/220px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/330px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cold_War_Map_1980.svg/440px-Cold_War_Map_1980.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_Map_1980.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The world map of military alliances in 1980</div></div></div>\n<p>In January 1977, four years prior to becoming president, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> bluntly stated, in a conversation with <a href="/wiki/Richard_V._Allen" title="Richard V. Allen">Richard V. Allen</a>, his basic expectation in relation to the Cold War. "My idea of American policy toward the Soviet Union is simple, and some would say simplistic," he said. "It is this: We win and they lose. What do you think of that?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> In 1980, <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> defeated Jimmy Carter in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1980" title="United States presidential election, 1980">1980 presidential election</a>, vowing to increase military spending and confront the Soviets everywhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> Both Reagan and new British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> denounced the Soviet Union and its ideology. Reagan labeled the Soviet Union an "<a href="/wiki/Evil_Empire_speech" title="Evil Empire speech">evil empire</a>" and predicted that Communism would be left on the "<a href="/wiki/Ash_heap_of_history" title="Ash heap of history">ash heap of history</a>," while Thatcher inculpated the Soviets as "bent on world dominance."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._197_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._197-278">[278]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> In 1982 Reagan tried to cut off Moscow\'s access to hard currency by impeding its proposed gas line to Western Europe. It hurt the Soviet economy, but it also caused ill will among American allies in Europe who counted on that revenue. Reagan retreated on this issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup>\n</p><p>By early 1985, Reagan\'s anti-communist position had developed into a stance known as the new <a href="/wiki/Reagan_Doctrine" title="Reagan Doctrine">Reagan Doctrine</a>&#8212;which, in addition to containment, formulated an additional right to subvert existing communist governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Graebner,_Burns_&amp;_Siracusa_2008,_76_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-Graebner,_Burns_&amp;_Siracusa_2008,_76-282">[282]</a></sup> Besides continuing Carter\'s policy of supporting the Islamic opponents of the Soviet Union and the Soviet-backed <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Party_of_Afghanistan" title="People\'s Democratic Party of Afghanistan">PDPA</a> government in Afghanistan, the CIA also sought to weaken the Soviet Union itself by promoting <a href="/wiki/Islamism" title="Islamism">Islamism</a> in the majority-Muslim <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Central_Asia" title="Soviet Central Asia">Central Asian Soviet Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh_1995,_130_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-Singh_1995,_130-283">[283]</a></sup> Additionally, the CIA encouraged anti-communist Pakistan\'s ISI to train Muslims from around the world to participate in the <a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">jihad</a> against the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Singh_1995,_130_283-1"><a href="#cite_note-Singh_1995,_130-283">[283]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish_Solidarity_movement_and_martial_law">Polish Solidarity movement and martial law</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">Solidarity (Polish trade union)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_Poland" title="Martial law in Poland">Martial law in Poland</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_reaction_to_the_Polish_crisis_of_1980%E2%80%9381" title="Soviet reaction to the Polish crisis of 1980&#8211;81">Soviet reaction to the Polish crisis of 1980&#8211;81</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> provided a moral focus for <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communism</a>; a visit to his native Poland in 1979 stimulated a religious and nationalist resurgence centered on the <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">Solidarity movement</a> that galvanized opposition and may have led to his <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II_assassination_attempt" title="Pope John Paul II assassination attempt">attempted assassination</a> two years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup>\nIn December 1981, Poland\'s <a href="/wiki/Wojciech_Jaruzelski" title="Wojciech Jaruzelski">Wojciech Jaruzelski</a> reacted to the crisis by imposing <a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_Poland" title="Martial law in Poland">a period of martial law</a>. Reagan imposed economic sanctions on Poland in response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis219_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis219-285">[285]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Suslov" title="Mikhail Suslov">Mikhail Suslov</a>, the Kremlin\'s top ideologist, advised Soviet leaders not to intervene if Poland fell under the control of Solidarity, for fear it might lead to heavy economic sanctions, resulting in a catastrophe for the Soviet economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis219_285-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis219-285">[285]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_and_US_military_and_economic_issues">Soviet and US military and economic issues</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further
