information: <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation" title="Era of Stagnation">Era of Stagnation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defense_Initiative" title="Strategic Defense Initiative">Strategic Defense Initiative</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS-20_Saber" title="SS-20 Saber">SS-20 Saber</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MGM-31_Pershing" title="MGM-31 Pershing">MGM-31 Pershing</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="555" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg/220px-US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg/330px-US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg/440px-US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_and_USSR_nuclear_stockpiles.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US and USSR/Russian nuclear weapons stockpiles, 1945&#8211;2006</div></div></div>\n<p>Moscow had built up a military that consumed as much as 25&#160;percent of the Soviet Union\'s gross national product at the expense of <a href="/wiki/Consumer_goods_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Consumer goods in the Soviet Union">consumer goods</a> and investment in civilian sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber_2002,_p._332_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber_2002,_p._332-286">[286]</a></sup> Soviet spending on the <a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">arms race</a> and other Cold War commitments both caused and exacerbated deep-seated structural problems in the Soviet system,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> which experienced at least <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation" title="Era of Stagnation">a decade of economic stagnation</a> during the late Brezhnev years.\n</p><p>Soviet investment in the defense sector was not driven by military necessity, but in large part by the interests of <a href="/wiki/Nomenklatura" title="Nomenklatura">massive party and state bureaucracies</a> dependent on the sector for their own power and privileges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces" title="Soviet Armed Forces">Soviet Armed Forces</a> became the largest in the world in terms of the numbers and types of weapons they possessed, in the number of troops in their ranks, and in the sheer size of their <a href="/wiki/Military%E2%80%93industrial_complex" title="Military&#8211;industrial complex">military&#8211;industrial base</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Odom_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-Odom-289">[289]</a></sup> However, the quantitative advantages held by the Soviet military often concealed areas where the Eastern Bloc dramatically lagged behind the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Persian Gulf War</a> demonstrated how the <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_armour" title="Vehicle armour">armor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fire-control_system" title="Fire-control system">fire control systems</a> and firing range of the Soviet Union\'s most common main battle tank, the <a href="/wiki/T-72" title="T-72">T-72</a>, were drastically inferior to the American <a href="/wiki/M1_Abrams" title="M1 Abrams">M1 Abrams</a>, yet the USSR fielded almost three times as many T-72s as the US deployed M1s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2800" data-file-width="1890" decoding="async" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg/170px-SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg/255px-SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg/340px-SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SDIO_Delta_Star.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Delta 183 launch vehicle lifts off, carrying the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defense_Initiative" title="Strategic Defense Initiative">Strategic Defense Initiative</a> sensor experiment "Delta Star".</div></div></div>\n<p>By the early 1980s, the USSR had built up a military arsenal and army surpassing that of the United States. Soon after the Soviet invasion of Afghanistan, president Carter began massively building up the United States military. This buildup was accelerated by the Reagan administration, which increased the military spending from 5.3 percent of GNP in 1981 to 6.5 percent in 1986,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> the largest peacetime defense buildup in United States history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tensions continued to intensify as Reagan revived the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B-1_Lancer" title="B-1 Lancer">B-1 Lancer</a> program, which had been canceled by the Carter administration, produced <a href="/wiki/LGM-118_Peacekeeper" title="LGM-118 Peacekeeper">LGM-118 Peacekeeper</a> missiles,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> installed US cruise missiles in Europe, and announced the experimental <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defense_Initiative" title="Strategic Defense Initiative">Strategic Defense Initiative</a>, dubbed "Star Wars" by the media, a defense program to shoot down missiles in mid-flight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShieldSpace?_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-ShieldSpace?-295">[295]</a></sup> The Soviets deployed <a href="/wiki/RSD-10_Pioneer" title="RSD-10 Pioneer">RSD-10 Pioneer</a> <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">ballistic missiles</a> targeting Western Europe, and NATO decided, under the impetus of the Carter presidency, to deploy <a href="/wiki/MGM-31_Pershing" title="MGM-31 Pershing">MGM-31 Pershing</a> and cruise missiles in Europe, primarily West Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> This deployment placed missiles just 10&#160;minutes\' striking distance from Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Reagan\'s military buildup, the Soviet Union did not respond by further building its military,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> because the enormous military expenses, along with inefficient <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned manufacturing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Collectivization in the Soviet Union">collectivized agriculture</a>, were already a heavy burden for the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Economy of the Soviet Union">Soviet economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaidar,_Yegor_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaidar,_Yegor-299">[299]</a></sup> At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> increased oil production,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> even as other non-OPEC nations were increasing production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIA_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-301">[301]</a></sup> These developments contributed to the <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">1980s oil glut</a>, which affected the Soviet Union as oil was the main source of Soviet export revenues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber_2002,_p._332_286-1"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber_2002,_p._332-286">[286]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaidar,_Yegor_299-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaidar,_Yegor-299">[299]</a></sup> Issues with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Command_economy" title="Command economy">command economics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardt1_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-hardt1-302">[302]</a></sup> oil price decreases and large military expenditures gradually brought the Soviet economy to stagnation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaidar,_Yegor_299-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gaidar,_Yegor-299">[299]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1985_CPA_5685.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="956" data-file-width="674" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/1985_CPA_5685.jpg/170px-1985_CPA_5685.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/1985_CPA_5685.jpg/255px-1985_CPA_5685.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/1985_CPA_5685.jpg/340px-1985_CPA_5685.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1985_CPA_5685.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>After ten-year-old American <a href="/wiki/Samantha_Smith" title="Samantha Smith">Samantha Smith</a> wrote a letter to <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Andropov" title="Yuri Andropov">Yuri Andropov</a> expressing her fear of nuclear war, Andropov invited Smith to the Soviet Union.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 1 September 1983, the Soviet Union shot down <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air_Lines_Flight_007" title="Korean Air Lines Flight 007">Korean Air Lines Flight 007</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> with 269 people aboard, including sitting Congressman <a href="/wiki/Larry_McDonald" title="Larry McDonald">Larry McDonald</a>, an action which Reagan characterized as a "massacre". The airliner had violated Soviet airspace just past the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin Island</a> near <a href="/wiki/Moneron_Island" title="Moneron Island">Moneron Island</a>, and the Soviets treated the unidentified aircraft as an intruding U.S. spy plane. The incident increased support for military deployment, overseen by Reagan, which stood in place until the later accords between Reagan and Mikhail Gorbachev.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DoernerFive_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-DoernerFive-303">[303]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Able_Archer_83" title="Able Archer 83">Able Archer 83</a> exercise in November 1983, a realistic simulation of a coordinated NATO nuclear release, was perhaps the most dangerous moment since the Cuban Missile Crisis, as the Soviet leadership feared that a nuclear attack might be imminent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup>\n</p><p>American domestic public concerns about intervening in foreign conflicts persisted from the end of the Vietnam War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber323_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber323-305">[305]</a></sup> The Reagan administration emphasized the use of quick, low-cost <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">counter-insurgency</a> tactics to intervene in foreign conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber323_305-1"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber323-305">[305]</a></sup> In 1983, the Reagan administration intervened in the multisided <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">Lebanese Civil War</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" title="Invasion of Grenada">invaded</a> <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_United_States_bombing_of_Libya" title="1986 United States bombing of Libya">bombed</a> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi#Great_Socialist_People\'s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya_(1977&#8211;2011)" title="History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">Libya</a> and backed the Central American <a href="/wiki/Contras" title="Contras">Contras</a>, anti-communist paramilitaries seeking to overthrow the Soviet-aligned <a href="/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front" title="Sandinista National Liberation Front">Sandinista</a> government in Nicaragua.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._212_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._212-132">[132]</a></sup> While Reagan\'s interventions against Grenada and Libya were popular in the United States, his backing of the Contra rebels was <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Contra_affair" title="Iran&#8211;Contra affair">mired in controversy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reagan_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reagan-306">[306]</a></sup> The Reagan administration\'s backing of the military government of <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Guatemalan_Civil_War" title="Guatemalan Civil War">Guatemalan Civil War</a>, in particular the regime of <a href="/wiki/Efra%C3%ADn_R%C3%ADos_Montt" title="Efra&#237;n R&#237;os Montt">Efra&#237;n R&#237;os Montt</a>, was also controversial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Meanwhile, the Soviets incurred high costs for their own foreign interventions. Although Brezhnev was convinced in 1979 that the <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War" title="Soviet&#8211;Afghan War">Soviet war in Afghanistan</a> would be brief, Muslim guerrillas, aided by the U.S., China, Britain, Saudi Arabia and Pakistan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Warren_272-1"><a href="#cite_note-Warren-272">[272]</a></sup> waged a fierce resistance against the invasion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber314_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber314-308">[308]</a></sup> The Kremlin sent nearly 100,000 troops to support its puppet regime in Afghanistan, leading many outside observers to dub the war "the Soviets\' Vietnam".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber314_308-1"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber314-308">[308]</a></sup> However, Moscow\'s quagmire in Afghanistan was far more disastrous for the Soviets than Vietnam had been for the Americans because the conflict coincided with a period of internal decay and domestic crisis in the Soviet system.\n</p><p>A senior <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> official predicted such an outcome as early as 1980, positing that the invasion resulted in part from a "domestic crisis within the Soviet <span class="nowrap">system. ... It</span> may be that the thermodynamic law of <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">entropy</a> <span class="nowrap">has ... caught</span> up with the Soviet system, which now seems to expend more energy on simply maintaining its equilibrium than on improving itself. We could be seeing a period of foreign movement at a time of internal decay".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dobrynin_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dobrynin-309">[309]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Final_years_.281985.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_years_(1985&#8211;1991)">Final years (1985&#8211;1991)</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_(1985%E2%80%931991)" title="Cold War (1985&#8211;1991)">Cold War (1985&#8211;1991)</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Gorbachev.27s_reforms"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gorbachev\'s_reforms">Gorbachev\'s reforms</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">Perestroika</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">Glasnost</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3144" data-file-width="5100" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg/220px-Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg/330px-Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg/440px-Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mikhail Gorbachev and Ronald Reagan sign the <a href="/wiki/Intermediate-Range_Nuclear_Forces_Treaty" title="Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty">INF Treaty</a> at the White House, 1987.</div></div></div>\n<p>By the time the comparatively youthful <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> became <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">General Secretary</a> in 1985,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_p._197_278-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_p._197-278">[278]</a></sup> the Soviet economy was stagnant and faced a sharp fall in foreign currency earnings as a result of the downward slide in oil prices in the 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber331_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber331-311">[311]</a></sup> These issues prompted Gorbachev to investigate measures to revive the ailing state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber331_311-1"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber331-311">[311]</a></sup>\n</p><p>An ineffectual start led to the conclusion that deeper structural changes were necessary, and in June 1987 Gorbachev announced an agenda of economic reform called <i><a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a></i>, or restructuring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis231_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis231-312">[312]</a></sup> Perestroika relaxed the <a href="/wiki/Production_quota" title="Production quota">production quota</a> system, allowed private ownership of businesses and paved the way for foreign investment. These measures were intended to redirect the country\'s resources from costly Cold War military commitments to more productive areas in the civilian sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis231_312-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis231-312">[312]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite initial skepticism in the West, the new Soviet leader proved to be committed to reversing the Soviet Union\'s deteriorating economic condition instead of continuing the arms race with the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Palmowski_148-3"><a href="#cite_note-Palmowski-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaFeber2002_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaFeber2002-313">[313]</a></sup> Partly as a way to fight off internal opposition from party cliques to his reforms, Gorbachev simultaneously introduced <i><a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a></i>, or openness, which increased freedom of the press and the transparency of state institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> <i>Glasnost</i> was intended to reduce the corruption at the top of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_party" title="Communist party">Communist Party</a> and moderate the <a href="/wiki/Abuse_of_power" title="Abuse of power">abuse of power</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Committee" title="Central Committee">Central Committee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> Glasnost also enabled increased contact between Soviet citizens and the western world, particularly with the United States, contributing to the accelerating <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="D&#233;tente">d&#233;tente</a> between the two nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thaw_in_relations">Thaw in relations</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk_Summit" title="Reykjav&#237;k Summit">Reykjav&#237;k Summit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intermediate-Range_Nuclear_Forces_Treaty" title="Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty">Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/START_I" title="START I">START I</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Final_Settlement_with_Respect_to_Germany" title="Treaty on the Final Settlement with Respect to Germany">Treaty on the Final Settlement with Respect to Germany</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1992" data-file-width="2958" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg/200px-Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg/300px-Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg/400px-Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bush_Gorba_P15623-25A.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The beginning of the 1990s brought a thaw in relations between the superpowers.</div></div></div>\n<p>In response to the Kremlin\'s military and <a href="/wiki/Concession_(politics)" title="Concession (politics)">political concessions</a>, Reagan agreed to renew talks on economic issues and the scaling-back of the arms race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis229_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis229-317">[317]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Summit_(1985)" title="Geneva Summit (1985)">summit</a> was held in November 1985 in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis229_317-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis229-317">[317]</a></sup> At one stage the two men, accompanied only by an interpreter, agreed in principle to reduce each country\'s nuclear arsenal by 50&#160;percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk_Summit" title="Reykjav&#237;k Summit">second summit</a> was held in October 1986 in <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav&#237;k">Reykjav&#237;k</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>. Talks went well until the focus shifted to Reagan\'s proposed Strategic Defense Initiative, which Gorbachev wanted eliminated. Reagan refused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> The negotiations failed, but the third summit in 1987 led to a breakthrough with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Intermediate-Range_Nuclear_Forces_Treaty" title="Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty">Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty</a> (INF). The INF treaty eliminated all nuclear-armed, ground-launched ballistic and cruise missiles with ranges between 500 and 5,500&#160;kilometers (300 to 3,400&#160;miles) and their infrastructure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fas_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-fas-320">[320]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ReaganBerlinWall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2009" data-file-width="2846" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/ReaganBerlinWall.jpg/220px-ReaganBerlinWall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/ReaganBerlinWall.jpg/330px-ReaganBerlinWall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/ReaganBerlinWall.jpg/440px-ReaganBerlinWall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ReaganBerlinWall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"<a href="/wiki/Tear_down_this_wall!" title="Tear down this wall!">Tear down this wall!</a>" speech: Reagan speaking in front of the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a>, 12 June 1987</div></div></div>\n<p>East&#8211;West tensions rapidly subsided through the mid-to-late 1980s, culminating with the final summit in Moscow in 1989, when Gorbachev and <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a> signed the <a href="/wiki/START_I" title="START I">START I</a> arms control treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> During the following year it became apparent to the Soviets that oil and gas subsidies, along with the cost of maintaining massive troops levels, represented a substantial economic drain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shearman76_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shearman76-322">[322]</a></sup> In addition, the security advantage of a buffer zone was recognised as irrelevant and the Soviets <a href="/wiki/Sinatra_Doctrine" title="Sinatra Doctrine">officially declared</a> that they would no longer intervene in the affairs of allied states in Central and Eastern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis248_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis248-323">[323]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1989, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_withdrawal_from_Afghanistan" title="Soviet withdrawal from Afghanistan">Soviet forces withdrew from Afghanistan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_pp._235&#8211;236_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_pp._235&#8211;236-324">[324]</a></sup> and by 1990 Gorbachev <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Final_Settlement_with_Respect_to_Germany" title="Treaty on the Final Settlement with Respect to Germany">consented</a> to <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shearman76_322-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shearman76-322">[322]</a></sup> as the only alternative was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiananmen_Square_protests_of_1989" title="Tiananmen Square protests of 1989">Tiananmen Square</a> scenario.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> When the Berlin Wall came down, Gorbachev\'s "<a href="/wiki/Common_European_Home" title="Common European Home">Common European Home</a>" concept began to take shape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 3 December 1989, Gorbachev and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" title="George H.W. Bush">George H.W. Bush</a> declared the Cold War over at the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Summit" title="Malta Summit">Malta Summit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cwover_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-cwover-327">[327]</a></sup> A year later, the two former rivals were partners in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a> against <a href="/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq" title="Ba\'athist Iraq">Iraq</a> (August 1990 &#8211; February 1991).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Europe_breaks_away">Eastern Europe breaks away</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">Revolutions of 1989</a></div>\n<p>By 1989, the Soviet alliance system was on the brink of collapse, and, deprived of Soviet military support, the communist leaders of the Warsaw Pact states were losing power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis_2005,_pp._235&#8211;236_324-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis_2005,_pp._235&#8211;236-324">[324]</a></sup> Grassroots organizations, such as Poland\'s <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">Solidarity</a> movement, rapidly gained ground with strong popular bases. In 1989, the communist governments in Poland and Hungary became the first to negotiate the organization of competitive elections. In Czechoslovakia and East Germany, mass protests unseated entrenched communist leaders. The communist regimes in Bulgaria and Romania also crumbled, in the latter case as the result of a <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Revolution" title="Romanian Revolution">violent uprising</a>. Attitudes had changed enough that U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/James_Baker" title="James Baker">James Baker</a> suggested that the American government would not be opposed to Soviet intervention in Romania, on behalf of the opposition, to prevent bloodshed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> The tidal wave of change culminated with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Berlin_Wall" title="Fall of the Berlin Wall">fall of the Berlin Wall</a> in November 1989, which symbolized the collapse of European communist governments and graphically ended the Iron Curtain divide of Europe. The <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">1989 revolutionary wave</a> swept across Central and Eastern Europe and peacefully overthrew all of the Soviet-style communist states: East Germany, Poland, Hungary, Czechoslovakia and Bulgaria;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> Romania was the only Eastern-bloc country to topple its communist regime violently and execute its head of state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_republics_break_away">Soviet republics break away</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Economy of the Soviet Union">Economy of the Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Way" title="Baltic Way">Baltic Way</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2624" data-file-width="3936" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg/220px-Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg/330px-Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg/440px-Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baltsk%C3%BD%C5%98et%C4%9Bz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The human chain in <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Way" title="Baltic Way">Baltic Way</a>, 23 August 1989</div></div></div>\n<p>In the USSR itself, <i>glasnost</i> weakened the bonds that held the Soviet Union together,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaddis248_323-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gaddis248-323">[323]</a></sup> and by February 1990, with the dissolution of the USSR looming, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party</a> was forced to surrender its 73-year-old monopoly on state power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> At the same time freedom of press and dissent allowed by <i>glasnost</i> and the festering "nationalities question" increasingly led the union\'s component republics to declare their autonomy from Moscow, with the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> withdrawing from the union entirely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_dissolution">Soviet dissolution</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Dissolution of the Soviet Union</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1982%E2%80%9391)" title="History of the Soviet Union (1982&#8211;91)">History of the Soviet Union (1982&#8211;91)</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Barricades" title="The Barricades">The Barricades</a>, <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d\'&#233;tat attempt">1991 Soviet coup d\'&#233;tat attempt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="1438" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_848095_Signing_the_Agreement_to_eliminate_the_USSR_and_establish_the_Commonwealth_of_Independent_States.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Leaders of the Soviet Republics</a> sign the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belovezha_Accords" title="Belovezha Accords">Belovezha Accords</a>, which eliminated the USSR and established the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> in 1991.</div></div></div>\n<p>Gorbachev\'s permissive attitude toward Central and Eastern Europe did not initially extend to Soviet territory; even Bush, who strove to maintain friendly relations, condemned the January 1991 killings in <a href="/wiki/The_Barricades" title="The Barricades">Latvia</a> and <a href="/wiki/January_Events_(Lithuania)" title="January Events (Lithuania)">Lithuania</a>, privately warning that economic ties would be frozen if the violence continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup> The USSR was fatally weakened by a <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d\'&#233;tat attempt">failed coup</a>, and a growing number of <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Soviet republics</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russia</a>, threatened to secede from the USSR. The <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, created on 21 December 1991, is viewed as a successor entity to the Soviet Union, but, according to Russia\'s leaders, its purpose was to "allow a civilized divorce" between the Soviet Republics and is comparable to a loose <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup> The USSR was declared officially dissolved on 26 December 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup>\n</p><p>U.S. President George H.W. Bush expressed his emotions: "The biggest thing that has happened in the world in my life, in our lives, is this: By the grace of God, America won the Cold War."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_the_Cold_War" title="Effects of the Cold War">Effects of the Cold War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frozen_conflict" title="Frozen conflict">Frozen conflict</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">Post-Soviet states</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_conflicts" title="Post-Soviet conflicts">Post-Soviet conflicts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_II" title="Cold War II">Cold War II</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_border_changes.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="599" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cold_War_border_changes.png/260px-Cold_War_border_changes.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cold_War_border_changes.png/390px-Cold_War_border_changes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cold_War_border_changes.png/520px-Cold_War_border_changes.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_border_changes.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Changes in national boundaries after the end of the Cold War</div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, Russia drastically cut <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">military spending</a>, and restructuring the economy left millions unemployed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aslund_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aslund-338">[338]</a></sup> The capitalist reforms culminated in a <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a> in the early 1990s more severe than the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> as experienced by the United States and Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nolan_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nolan-339">[339]</a></sup> In the 25 years following the end of the Cold War, only five or six of the post-communist states are on a path to joining the rich and capitalist world while most are falling behind, some to such an extent that it will take several decades to catch up to where they were before the collapse of communism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Cold War continues to influence world affairs. The post-Cold War world is considered to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unipolarity" title="Unipolarity">unipolar</a>, with the United States the sole remaining <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> The Cold War defined the political role of the United States after World War&#160;II&#8212;by 1989 the United States had military alliances with 50 countries, with 526,000 troops stationed abroad,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frontline_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frontline-345">[345]</a></sup> with 326,000 in Europe (two-thirds of which were in west Germany)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> and 130,000 in Asia (mainly <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frontline_345-1"><a href="#cite_note-Frontline-345">[345]</a></sup> The Cold War also marked the zenith of peacetime <a href="/wiki/Military%E2%80%93industrial_complex" title="Military&#8211;industrial complex">military&#8211;industrial complexes</a>, especially in the United States, and large-scale <a href="/wiki/History_of_military_technology" title="History of military technology">military funding of science</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calhoun_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-Calhoun-347">[347]</a></sup> These complexes, though their origins may be found as early as the 19th century, snowballed considerably during the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-348"><a href="#cite_note-348">[348]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1245" data-file-width="1245" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif/220px-Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif/330px-Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif/440px-Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Enlargement_of_the_European_Union_77.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Since the end of the Cold War, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> has <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">expanded eastwards</a> into the former Warsaw Pact and parts of the former Soviet Union.</div></div></div>\n<p>Cumulative U.S. military expenditures throughout the entire Cold War amounted to an estimated $8&#160;trillion. Further nearly 100,000 Americans lost their lives in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam Wars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349">[349]</a></sup> Although Soviet casualties are difficult to estimate, as a share of their gross national product the financial cost for the Soviet Union was much higher than that incurred by the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[350]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to the loss of life by uniformed soldiers, millions died in the superpowers\' <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a> around the globe, most notably in Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> Most of the proxy wars and subsidies for local conflicts ended along with the Cold War; interstate wars, ethnic wars, revolutionary wars, as well as refugee and displaced persons crises have declined sharply in the post-Cold War years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_352-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-352">[352]</a></sup> Left over from the Cold War are <a href="/wiki/Numbers_station" title="Numbers station">numbers stations</a>, which are <a href="/wiki/Shortwave_radio" title="Shortwave radio">shortwave radio</a> stations thought to be used to broadcast covert messages, some of which can still be heard today.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>However, the aftermath of the Cold War is not always easily erased, as many of the economic and social tensions that were exploited to fuel Cold War competition in parts of the Third World remain acute. The breakdown of state control in a number of areas formerly ruled by communist governments produced new civil and ethnic conflicts, particularly in the former <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>. In Central and Eastern Europe, the end of the Cold War has ushered in an era of <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a> and an increase in the number of <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democracies</a>, while in other parts of the world, such as Afghanistan, independence was accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Failed_state" title="Failed state">state failure</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_267-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-267">[267]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_during_the_Cold_War" title="Culture during the Cold War">Culture during the Cold War</a></div>\n<p>During the Cold War itself, with the United States and the Soviet Union invested heavily in propaganda designed to influence the hearts and minds of people around the world, especially using motion pictures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-353"><a href="#cite_note-353">[353]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2015)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The Cold War endures as a popular topic reflected extensively in entertainment media, and continuing to the present with numerous post-1991 Cold War-themed feature films, novels, television, and other media.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2013, a KGB-sleeper-agents-living-next-door action drama series, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Americans_(2013_TV_series)" title="The Americans (2013 TV series)">The Americans</a></i>, set in the early 1980s, was ranked #6 on the <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> annual Best New TV Shows list; its six-season run concluded in May 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic-americans_354-0"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-americans-354">[354]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355">[355]</a></sup> At the same time, movies like <i><a href="/wiki/Crimson_Tide_(film)" title="Crimson Tide (film)">Crimson Tide</a></i> (1995) are shown in their entirety to educate college students about the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-356"><a href="#cite_note-356">[356]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historiography">Historiography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_the_Cold_War" title="Historiography of the Cold War">Historiography of the Cold War</a></div>\n<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;">\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_United_States_history" title="Timeline of United States history">Timeline</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Periods_in_US_history" title="Template:Periods in US history"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Periods_in_US_history" title="Template talk:Periods in US history"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Periods_in_US_history&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>As soon as the term "Cold War" was popularized to refer to post-war tensions between the United States and the Soviet Union, interpreting the course and origins of the conflict has been a source of heated controversy among historians, political scientists, and journalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nashel_357-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nashel-357">[357]</a></sup> In particular, historians have sharply disagreed as to who was responsible for the breakdown of Soviet&#8211;US relations after the Second World War; and whether the conflict between the two superpowers was inevitable, or could have been avoided.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brinkley_358-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brinkley-358">[358]</a></sup> Historians have also disagreed on what exactly the Cold War was, what the sources of the conflict were, and how to disentangle patterns of action and reaction between the two sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_267-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-267">[267]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although explanations of the origins of the conflict in academic discussions are complex and diverse, several general schools of thought on the subject can be identified. Historians commonly speak of three differing approaches to the study of the Cold War: "orthodox" accounts, "revisionism", and "post-revisionism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calhoun_347-1"><a href="#cite_note-Calhoun-347">[347]</a></sup>\n</p><p>"Orthodox" accounts place responsibility for the Cold War on the Soviet Union and its expansion further into Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calhoun_347-2"><a href="#cite_note-Calhoun-347">[347]</a></sup> "Revisionist" writers place more responsibility for the breakdown of post-war peace on the United States, citing a range of US efforts to isolate and confront the Soviet Union well before the end of World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calhoun_347-3"><a href="#cite_note-Calhoun-347">[347]</a></sup> "Post-revisionists" see the events of the Cold War as more nuanced, and attempt to be more balanced in determining what occurred during the Cold War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calhoun_347-4"><a href="#cite_note-Calhoun-347">[347]</a></sup> Much of the historiography on the Cold War weaves together two or even all three of these broad categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byrd_47-7"><a href="#cite_note-Byrd-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote (2018). <a class="external text" href="https://press.princeton.edu/titles/11135.html" rel="nofollow"><i>The Killing Season: A History of the Indonesian Massacres, 1965&#8211;66</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University_Press" title="Princeton University Press">Princeton University Press</a>. p.&#160;203. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4008-8886-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4008-8886-3">978-1-4008-8886-3</a>. <q>a US Embassy official in Jakarta, Robert Martens, had supplied the Indonesian Army with lists containing the names of thousands of PKI officials in the months after the alleged coup attempt. According to the journalist Kathy Kadane, "As many as 5,000 names were furnished over a period of months to the Army there, and the Americans later checked off the names of those who had been killed or captured." Despite Martens later denials of any such intent, these actions almost certainly aided in the death or detention of many innocent people. They also sent a powerful message that the US government agreed with and supported the army\'s campaign against the PKI, even as that campaign took its terrible toll in human lives.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Killing+Season%3A+A+History+of+the+Indonesian+Massacres%2C+1965%E2%80%9366&amp;rft.pages=203&amp;rft.pub=Princeton+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2018&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4008-8886-3&amp;rft.aulast=Robinson&amp;rft.aufirst=Geoffrey+B.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fpress.princeton.edu%2Ftitles%2F11135.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACold+War"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-219"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-219">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Simpson, Bradley (2010). <a class="external text" href="https://www.sup.org/books/title/?id=7853" rel="nofollow"><i>Economists with Guns: Authoritarian Development and U.S.&#8211;Indonesian Relations, 1960&#8211;1968</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University_Press" title="Stanford University Press">Stanford University Press</a>. p.&#160;193. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8047-7182-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8047-7182-5">978-0-8047-7182-5</a>. <q>Washington did everything in its power to encourage and facilitate the army-led massacre of alleged PKI members, and U.S. officials worried only that the killing of the party\'s unarmed supporters might not go far enough, permitting Sukarno to return to power and frustrate the [Johnson] Administration\'s emerging plans for a post-Sukarno Indonesia. This was efficacious terror, an essential building block of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoliberal" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> policies that the West would attempt to impose on Indonesia after Sukarno\'s ouster.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Economists+with+Guns%3A+Authoritarian+Development+and+U.S.%E2%80%93Indonesian+Relations%2C+1960%E2%80%931968&amp;rft.pages=193&amp;rft.pub=Stanford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8047-7182-5&amp;rft.aulast=Simpson&amp;rft.aufirst=Bradley&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.sup.org%2Fbooks%2Ftitle%2F%3Fid%3D7853&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACold+War"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-220"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-220">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Kai Thaler (2 December 2015). <a class="external text" href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/monkey-cage/wp/2015/12/02/50-years-ago-today-the-u-s-embassy-endorsed-mass-killings-in-indonesia-heres-what-that-means-for-today/" rel="nofollow">50 years ago today, American diplomats endorsed mass killings in Indonesia.
